younge students as are desi&shy; 
rous to attaine the know&#173;

the olde Te&#173;

<section type="Lexicon">
<wordgroup1 type="a">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abatement(n)" lexeme="writ(n)">&#182; Abatement of a writ 
or plaint,</form>
<xpln lang="en">ABatement of a 
writ or plaint, 
is wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> an acti&#173;
on is brought by writ 
or plaint, wherein is 
lack of sufficient &#38; good 
matter, or els the mat&#173;
ter alleaged, is not cer&#173;
teinly set downe, or if 
the plaintife or defen&#173;
d<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t, or place, are misna&#173;
med, or of ther appeare 
variance betwene the 
writ and the specialty, 
or recorde, or that the 
writ or the declaration 
be vncerten, or for death 
of the plaintif or def<expan type="e+_">en</expan>&#173;
d<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t, &#38; for diuers other 
lyke causes which I 
omyt of purpose, for 
thereof alone, a man 
might make a large dis<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
course, and I determin 
to satisfie you (good 
Brother Nicholas) as 
wel as I may, with as 
much breuitie, and as 
litle trouble to my self 
</page>
 
<page sig="1v">
as I can, then vppon 
those defaults, the de&#173;
fendant may pray that 
the writte or plaint 
may abate, that is to 
say, that the plaintife 
suit against him may 
cease for that time, and 
that he shall begyn a&#173;
gaine his suit, &#38; bring 
a new writ or plaint 
if he bee so dysposed 
to do.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abatement(n)" lexeme="land(n)">&#182; Abatement in landes.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ABatement in l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
or tenementes, is 
when a man dyeth 
seised of landes or te&#173;
nementes, and a stran&#173;
ger, that is to say, one 
that hath no right en&#173;
treth into the same 
landes or tenementes, 
before the heir maketh 
his entrie, this entrie 
of the str<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ger is called 
an abatement, &#38; he an 
abatour. But if the 
heire enter first after <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
death of his a<expan type="u+_">un</expan>cestor, 
</page>
 
<page sig="2r">
and the straunger en&#173;
ter vpon the possession 
of the heire, this en&#173;
trie of the straunger, 
is a disseisine to the 
heire.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abbot(n)">&#182; Abbot.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="convent(n)">ABbot, was the so&#173;
ueraigne head or 
chief of those hou&#173;
ses of Popish Reli&#173;
gion, whiche when 
they stoode were cal&#173;
led Abbeis, and this 
Abbot together wyth 
the Monkes of the 
same house, who were 
called the Couent, 
made a corporation.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abettor(n)">&#182; Abbettors.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ABbettors are in di&#173;
uers cases diuersly 
taken, one kind of ab&#173;
bettors are they that 
maliciouslye without 
iust cause or desert do 
procure other to sue 
fals appeals of murder 
</page>
 
<page sig="2v">
or felony, against men, 
to the ent<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t to trouble 
and greue them, and to 
brynge them into in&#173;
famye and sclaunder. 
Abbettors in murder, 
are those that com&#173;
maund, procure, coun&#173;
sell, or comfort others 
to murder. And in 
some case, such abbet&#173;
tors shall bee taken as 
principals, and in some 
case but as Accessories 
So in other felonies. 
And theyr presence at 
the deede doing, &#38; theyr 
abs<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ce, maketh a diffe&#173;
r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ce in the case. There 
are abbettors also in 
Treason, but they are 
in case as principalls, 
for in Treason there 
are no accessories.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abeyance(n)">&#182; Abeiance.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="power(n)" lexeme="understanding(n)" lexeme="cloud(n)">ABeyance is when 
a leas is made for 
terme of life, the re&#173;
maynder to the right 
heires of I. S. which 
</page>
 
<page sig="3r">
I.S. is lyuing at the 
tyme of the graunt: 
Now this graunt of 
remainder passeth from 
the grauntor present&#173;
lye, yet it vesteth not 
presently, nor taketh 
holde in the grauntee, 
that is to say, the right 
heire of I. S. but is 
said to be in Abeiance, 
or as the Logyciens 
terme it in power, or 
in vnderstanding, and 
as we say in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> clouds. 
That is to witte, in 
the c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>sideration of the 
lawe. That if I. S. 
dye, leauing a ryght 
heire lyuing, and ly&#173;
uing the lessee for lyfe, 
then this is a good re&#173;
mainder, and now ves&#173;
teth and commeth into 
that right heyre, in 
such sort, as that hee 
may graunt, forfait, or 
otherwise dyspose the 
same, and ceaseth to be 
any more in abeyance, 
for <expan type="y+t">that</expan> there is one now 
of abilitye to take it 
</page>
 
<page sig="3v">
because that I. S. is 
dead, and hath left a 
right heire in lyfe, 
which coulde not bee 
lyuing I.S. for that 
duringe his life, none 
could properly be said 
his heire. Also if a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>
be patron of a church, 
and presenteth one to 
the same: Now is the 
fee in the person, but if 
the person dye, and the 
church is become void, 
then is the fee in abey&#173;
ance, vntill there bee a 
new person presented, 
for the patron hath 
not the fee, but onely 
the right to present, 
and the fee is in the in<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cumbent that is pre&#173;
sented, and after hys 
death, it is in no body 
but in abeyance tyll 
there bee a new in&#173;
cumbent, as is afore&#173;
saide.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abishersing(n)">&#182; Abishersing.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="4r">
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="mishersing(n)" lexeme="transumption(n)">ABishersing (and in 
some copyes Mis&#173;
hersing,) that is to be 
quite of amercementes 
before whom soeuer 
of transumption pro&#173;
ued.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abjuration(n)">&#182; Abiuration.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ABiuration is an 
othe that a manne 
or woman shall take, 
when they haue com&#173;
mitted Felonie, and 
flie to the Church or 
church yarde for safe&#173;
garde of their lyues, 
choosing rather perpe&#173;
tuall banishment out 
of the Realme, then to 
stand to the Law, &#38; to 
be tried of the felony. 
And this lawe was 
instituted by Saynt 
Edward the Confes&#173;
sour a Kinge of thys 
realme before the con&#173;
quest, &#38; was grounded 
vpon the law of mer&#173;
cie, &#38; for the loue and 
</page>
 
<page sig="4v">
reuerence, no doubt, 
that hee and other hys 
successors did beare vn<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
to the house of God, 
or place of prayer and 
administration of hys 
woord and sacramen&#173;
tes, which wee cal the 
church. But how vn&#173;
comely a thing it was 
or is, and how farre 
from the nature of the 
house of God, to make 
her a succourer and de&#173;
f<expan type="e+_">en</expan>der of horrible mur&#173;
ferers &#38; theeues. You 
may consider (brother 
Nicholas) and the ra&#173;
ther when you remem&#173;
ber what our Sauy&#173;
our Christ saide, re&#173;
preh<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ding the Iewes, 
and paraduenture also 
prophesinge of thys. 
My house shalbe cal&#173;
led the house of praier, 
but you haue made it a 
denne of theeues.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="abridgement(n)" lexeme="plaint(n)" lexeme="demand(n)">&#182; Abridgement of a plaint 
or demaund.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="5r">
<xpln lang="en">ABridgement of a 
plaint or demaund 
is wher one brin&#173;
geth an Assise, writte 
of dower, writte of 
warde, or such lyke, 
where the writ is,<term lang="la">de 
libero tenemento</term>, as in 
a writte of dower, the 
writ is,<term lang="la">Rationabilem 
dotem que eam contingit 
de libero tenemento W.</term>
her husband. And in a 
writte of Warde the 
writte is,<term lang="la">Custod' ter&#173;
rarum &#38; her&ecedil;d' &#38;c.</term> And 
the plaintyfe or de&#173;
mandant demaundeth 
dyuers acres or par&#173;
cells of lande, and the 
tenant pleadeth Non&#173;
tenure or iointenancy, 
or some other such like 
plee, to parcell of the 
land demaunded, in a&#173;
batement of the writ: 
then the plaintif or de&#173;
mandant, may abridge 
hys plaint or demaund 
to that parcel, that is 
to say, hee may leaue 
that part out and pray 
</page>
 
<page sig="5v">
that the tenaunt shall 
aunsweare the rest to 
which he hath not yet 
pleded any thing. The 
cause is, for that in 
such writs <expan type="y+e">the</expan> certein&#173;
tye is not set downe, 
but the demaund run&#173;
neth generally<term lang="la">de libe&#173;
ro tenemento</term>, and not&#173;
withstanding the de&#173;
m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>dant hath abridged 
his plaint or demaund 
in part, yet the writte 
remaineth good stil,<term lang="la">de 
libero tenemento</term> for the 
rest.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acceptance(n)">&#182; Acceptance.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACceptance is a ta&#173;
king in good part, 
and as it were an a&#173;
greeing vnto some act 
done before, whych 
might haue ben vndon 
and auoyded (if such 
accept<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce had not ben) 
by him or them that so 
accepted. As for exam&#173;
ple, if an Abbot lease 
lande of his house for 
</page>
 
<page sig="6r">
terme of yeares, re&#173;
seruinge rent and dy&#173;
eth, and after an o&#173;
ther is made Abbot, 
who accepteth, that 
is to say, taketh or 
receyueth the rente 
when it is due, and 
ought to bee payed: 
Now by this accep&#173;
taunce the lease is 
made perfect and good, 
which els the Abbot 
myght very well haue 
auoyded and made 
frustrate. The lyke 
law is, if a man and 
his wife seised of land 
in the ryght of the 
wyfe ioyne and make 
a lease or feoffement 
reseruinge rent, and 
the husbande dyeth, 
shee accepteth or recei&#173;
ueth the rent, by 
which the feoffement 
or lease is made per&#173;
fecte and good, and 
shal barre her to bring 
her writte called<term lang="la">Cui 
in vita.</term></xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="6v">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="accessory(n)">&#182; Accessories.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACcessories are in 
two sorts, the one 
before the offence, 
the other after the of&#173;
fence is done. 
 
Accessorie before the 
fact, or offence, is hee 
that <emend err="commanndeth">commaundeth</emend> or 
procureth an other to 
doe felonie, and is not 
there present him selfe 
when the other doth it 
but if he be pres<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t, then 
he is also principal. 
 
Accessory after the of&#173;
fence or fact, is he that 
receyueth, fauoureth, 
or aideth, a felon, know<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ing well of the deede 
that he hath done. 
 
Also one may be acces<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
sorie to an accessory, as 
if one feloniously re&#173;
ceyue an other that is 
accessorie of a felonie, 
there the receiuer is an 
accessorie.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="7r">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="action(n)">&#182; Accion.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACcion is a suite 
geeuen by the law 
to recouer a thing, 
as an action of debte 
and such like.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="action(n)" lexeme="personal(n)">&#182; Accions personals.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACcions personals 
bee such accions 
whereby a manne 
claymeth debt, or o&#173;
ther goodes or cattell, 
or dammage for them, 
or damages for wrong 
done to his person.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="action(n)" lexeme="popular(a)">&#182; Accion populer.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACcion populer is 
an accion which is 
geeuen vppon the 
breach of some Penal 
statute; which action 
euery man that wyll 
may sue for him selfe, 
and the Queene, by 
information or other&#173;
wise, as the statute al&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="7v">
loweth and the case 
requyreth. And of 
these actions there bee 
an infinite number, but 
one for example is, 
when any of the iurie 
that are impanelled &#38; 
sworn to passe betwen 
party and party indif&#173;
ferently, do take any 
thing of the one side or 
other, or of both par&#173;
ties, to say their ver&#173;
dicts on that side: then 
any man that wil <expan type="w+t">with</expan>in 
the yeare next follow&#173;
inge the offence made, 
may sue a writ called 
<term lang="la">Decies tantum</term> agaynst 
him or them that so 
did take to geeue their 
verdict, &#38; because that 
this action is not gee&#173;
uen to one man specy&#173;
ally but generally to 
the Queenes people 
that wyll sue, it is 
called an actyon po&#173;
puler.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="action(n)" lexeme="real(a)">&#182; Actions reals.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="8r">
<xpln lang="en">ACtions reals, bee 
such actions where 
by the demaundaunt 
claymeth title to any 
landes or tenementes, 
rentes, or common, in 
fee simple, fee taile, or 
for terme of life.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="accord(n)">&#182; Accorde.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACcord is an agree&#173;
ment betwene two 
at the least, eyther to 
satisfie an offence, that 
the one hath made to 
the other. Or els it is 
a contract with diuers 
articles to bee done, 
some on the one part, 
and some on the other, 
where there shalbe one 
thinge for an other &#38;c. 
The firste is, when 
a manne hath done a 
trespas, or such like 
vnto an other for the 
which hee hath agreed 
with hym, satisfied 
and contented hym, 
with some recompence 
alreadie executed and 
</page>
 
<page sig="8v">
done in deede. And be 
cause that this recom&#173;
pence, is a full satis&#173;
faction for the offence, 
it shalbe a good barre 
in the law, if the other 
should sue againe any 
action for the same 
trespas. The other is, 
when as I.S. letteth 
a chamber for yeres to 
H.G. &#38; it is farther a&#173;
greed betwene them, 
that the said H.G. shal 
be at boorde with the 
said I.S. and shal for 
the same chamber and 
boorde pay to the sayd 
I.S. a certein summe 
&#38;c. this is a contract &#38; 
accorde, with articles 
on both sides.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acquital(n)">&#182; Acquital.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="frankalmoign(n)">ACquital is where 
there is Lorde, 
mesne, and tenant, 
and the tenant holdeth 
of the Mesne certeyne 
landes or tenementes 
in frankalmoygne, 
</page>
 
<page sig="9r">
frankmariage or such 
lyke, and the mesne 
holdethe ouer also of 
the Lord paramount, 
(or aboue him. Nowe 
ought the mesne to ac&#173;
quite or discharge the 
tenant of all and eue&#173;
ry manner of seruice, 
that any other would 
haue or demaunde of 
hym concernynge the 
same landes or tene&#173;
mentes, for that the 
tenaunt must doo his 
seruyce to the mesne 
onely, and not to dy&#173;
uers Lordes for one 
tenement, or parcel of 
lande. The same lawe 
is where there is lord, 
mesne, and tenant, as 
aforesayde, and the 
mesne graunted to the 
tenant (vppon the te&#173;
nure made betweene 
them) to acquite, and 
dyscharge hym of all 
rentes seruyces, and 
such lyke. This dis&#173;
charge is called acqui&#173;
tall.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="9v">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="acquittance(n)">&#182; Acquitance.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACquitance is a dis&#173;
charge in writing, 
of a summe of money, 
or other duetie which 
ought to bee payde, 
or done. As if one be 
bounde to pay money 
vppon an obligation, 
or rent reserued vp&#173;
pon a lease, or such 
like, and the partye 
to whom the money, 
or duety shoulde bee 
payed, or done, vp&#173;
pon the resceit there&#173;
of, or vppon other a&#173;
greement betwene th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>
had, maketh a wri&#173;
ting, or bil of his hand, 
in discharge thereof, 
witnessing, that hee is 
payed, or otherwyse 
contented, and there&#173;
fore doth acquite, and 
discharge him of the 
same, which acquit<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce 
is such a discharge and 
barre in the law, that 
hee cannot demaunde, 
and recouer that s<expan type="u+_">um</expan>me 
or duety againe, con&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="10r">
trary therevnto if hee 
can shew <expan type="y+e">the</expan> acquit<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="addition(n)">&#182; Addicions.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ADdicyon is that, 
that is geuen vnto 
a man, but chiefely to 
the defendaunt, in ac&#173;
tyons where proces 
of outlawrie do lie, as 
in det, and such like, 
ouer and besides hys 
proper name and sir&#173;
name that is to say to 
shewe of what estate 
or degree, or myste&#173;
rye hee is, and of what 
Towne or Hamlet or 
County. 
 
Additions of Estate 
are these, yeoman, gen&#173;
tleman, Esquire, and 
such like. 
 
Addityons of de&#173;
gree are those that 
we cal names of dig&#173;
nitye, as Knight, 
Earls, Marques, and 
Duke. 
 
Additions of mistery 
</page>
 
<page sig="10v">
are suche, Scryue&#173;
ner, Painter, Mason, 
Carpenter, Tayler, 
Smith, &#38; so all other 
of like nature, for mis&#173;
tery is the craft or oc&#173;
cupati<expan type="o+_">on</expan>, wherby a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>
getteth his liuinge. 
 
Addicions of tow&#173;
nes, as Sale, Dale, 
and such, and so of the 
rest. 
 
And where a man 
hath houshold in two 
places, he shalbe said 
dwellinge in both of 
th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>, so that his addici&#173;
on in one of them doth 
suffice. 
 
And this was or&#173;
dayned by a Statute 
made in the first yere 
of H.5. cap. 5. to the 
intent that one man 
shoulde not bee gree&#173;
ued nor troubled by 
the vtlawry of an other, 
but that by reason of 
the certeine addicion, 
euery man myght bee 
certeinely knowne, and 
beare his own burden.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="11r">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="adjournment(n)">&#182; Adiournement.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ADiourement is 
when any Court 
is dissolued, and 
determyned, and 
determyned, and as&#173;
signed to bee kept a&#173;
gaine at an other place 
or time.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="administrator(n)">&#182; Administratour.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ADministratour is 
hee to whome the 
ordinary commit&#173;
teth theadministration 
of the goods of a dead 
man, for defaut of an 
executour, and an acti&#173;
on shal lie against him 
and for him as for an 
executour, &#38; he shalbee 
charged to the value of 
the goods of the dead 
man &#38; no further, if it 
be not by his own false 
plee, or for that that 
he hath wasted <expan type="y+e">the</expan> goods 
of the dead, but if thad<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ministratour die, hys 
executours be not ad&#173;
ministratours: but it 
behoueth <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Ordinarie 
</page>
 
<page sig="11v">
to commit a newe ad&#173;
ministration, but if a 
straunger that is not 
Administratour nor 
executoure take the 
goodes of the dead and 
minyster of hys owne 
wronge, hee shalbee 
charged and sued as 
an executour &#38; not as 
administratour in any 
action that is brought 
against hym by any 
creditour. But if the 
ordinary make a letter 
<term lang="la">ad colligendum bona de&#173;
f<expan type="u+_">un</expan>cti</term>, he that hath such 
a letter is not Admy&#173;
nistratour, but the ac&#173;
tion lyeth against the 
Ordinary, as wel as if 
he tooke the goodes to 
his owne hande, or 
by the hande of any of 
hys seruauntes by a&#173;
ny other commaunde&#173;
ment.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="act(n)">&#182; Actes.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ACtes of parliament 
are positiue lawes 
which consist of two 
</page>
 
<page sig="12r">
partes, that is to say, 
of the words of the act 
&#38; of the sence thereof, 
&#38; they both ioined to&#173;
gether make the lawe.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="admiral(n)">&#182; Admiral.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ADmirall is an offi&#173;
cer vnder <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Queene 
that hath aucthoritie, 
vpon the sea onely, to 
see the nauie repaired, 
&#38; maintained, to sup&#173;
presse, and chase away 
robbers, and rouers 
and to deale in mat&#173;
ters betweene party, 
and partie, concerning 
thinges done there, 
and for that purpose 
hath his court called 
the Admiralty: yet he 
may cause his Citati&#173;
on to be serued vppon 
the lande, and take the 
parties body, or goods, 
in execution vpon the 
land. And also he hath 
cognis<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce of the death 
or mayhem of man c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>&#173;
mitted in any great 
</page>
 
<page sig="12v">
ship fleetinge in great 
riuers in the land be&#173;
neth the bridges of <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
same next the sea, also 
to arrest ships in the 
great streames for the 
vyages of the Queene 
and Realme, and hath 
iurisdiction in the said 
streames duringe the 
same viages.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="advowson(n)">&#182; Aduowson.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="patron(n)">ADuowson is where 
a man, &#38; his heires 
haue right to present 
their Clerke to the or&#173;
dinarye, to a perso&#173;
nage, or other spiri&#173;
tuall benefice when it 
becommeth void. And 
hee that hath suche 
right to present, is cal&#173;
led patron.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="age prayer(n)">&#182; Age prier.</form>
<xpln lang="en">AGe prier is when 
an action is brought 
agaynst an infaunt, of 
landes that he hath by 
discent, there he shall 
shewe the matter to 
the court, and shal pray 
</page>
 
<page sig="13r">
that the action shall a&#173;
abide till his ful age of 
one and twenty yeres, 
and so by awarde of 
the court, the suit shal 
surcesse: But in a writ 
of Dower and in As&#173;
sise, &#38; also in such ac&#173;
tions where the infant 
c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>meth in of his owne 
wr<expan type="o+_">on</expan>g he shal not haue 
his age. 
 
Also note well, that 
there be many diuersi&#173;
ties of ages, for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> lord 
shal haue ayd of his te&#173;
naunt in socage for to 
marrye his daughter 
when the daughter of 
the Lorde is of thage 
of vij. yeres, and also 
aide for to make hys 
sonne &#38; heire knight, 
when he is of the age 
of vij. yeres. 
 
Also a woman which 
is maried at the age of 
ix. yeres if her husb<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d 
die seysed, shall haue 
dower and not before 
nine yeres. 
 
Also xiiij. yeres is the 
</page>
 
<page sig="13v">
age of a woman <expan type="y+t">that</expan> she 
shal not be in warde if 
she were of such age at 
the time of the death of 
her auncester, but if she 
were within the age 
of xiiij. yeares and in 
warde of the lord, th<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
she shalbe in ward till 
the age of xvi. yeres &#38; 
also xxi. yeares is the 
age of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> heire male to 
be in ward, &#38; after that 
out of warde, &#38; also it 
is the age of male and 
female to sue &#38; to bee 
sued of landes which 
they haue or claime by 
discent and to make al 
maner of contractes &#38; 
bargains &#38; not before: 
but if such an infaunt 
within the age of xxi. 
yeres geue his goods, &#38; 
the donee take them, he 
may haue an action of 
trespas, but otherwise 
it is if he deliuer them 
him selfe.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="agreement(n)">&#182; Agreement.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="forestaller(n)" lexeme="tass(n)">AGree<expan type="m+_">men</expan>t is after this 
sorte defined or ex&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="14r">
pounded in Master 
<term>Plowdens</term> Commenta&#173;
ries:<term lang="la">Aggreamentum</term>
is a worde compoun&#173;
ded of two wordes 
namely of<term lang="la">Aggrega&#173;
tio</term>, and<term lang="la">Mentium</term>, that 
is to saye agreement 
of minds, so <expan type="y+e">the</expan> agrem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
is a consent of mindes 
in some thinge done, 
or to bee done, and 
by drawynge toge&#173;
ther of the ij. wordes 
<term lang="la">Aggregatio</term>, and<term lang="la">Men&#173;
tium</term>, and by the has&#173;
tye and shorte pro&#173;
nouncinge of them, 
to witt,<term lang="la">Aggreamen&#173;
tum</term>, which is no other 
thing, then a ioining, 
putting, cupling, and 
knitting together of 
ij. or moe mindes in a&#173;
ny thinge done, or to 
be done. See after in 
Testament. 
 
And this agreement 
is in 3. maners. The j. 
is an agre<expan type="m+_">men</expan>t executed 
</page>
 
<page sig="14v">
all ready, at the bee&#173;
ginning. The seconde 
is an agreement after 
an act done, by an o&#173;
ther and is an agree&#173;
ment executed also. 
The third is an agre&#173;
ment executorie or to 
be done in time yet to 
come. The first, which 
is an agreement exe&#173;
cuted already at <expan type="y+e">the</expan> be&#173;
ginning, is such where 
of mencion is made in 
the statute of 25.E.3. 
ca. 3. of clothes, in the 
4. statute which saith, 
that <expan type="y+e">the</expan> goods &#38; things 
bought by forestallers 
being therof atta<expan type="i+_">in</expan>ted, 
shalbee forfayt to the 
Queene, if the buyer 
haue therof made gree 
wyth the seller, in 
which case, this word 
(Gree) which is other 
wise called agrement, 
shalbe vnderstood agre<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
m<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t executed, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is pai&#173;
m<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> things. The 
second maner of agre&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="15r">
ment, is where one 
doth a thinge, or acte, 
and an other agrees or 
aisentes thereto after&#173;
warde, as if one do a 
disseisin to my vse, and 
after I agree to it, now 
I shall bee a disseisour 
from the beginninge, 
and such agreement is 
an agreement after an 
act done. 
 
The thirde agree&#173;
ment is when bothe 
partyes at one tyme 
are agreed, that such a 
thinge shalbee done in 
tyme to come, and this 
agreement is executo&#173;
rie, in as much as the 
thing shalbe done af&#173;
ter, and yet there, their 
mindes agreed at one 
time, but because the 
perfourmance shalbee 
afterwarde, and so the 
thing vpon which the 
agreement was made 
remaynes to be done, 
that agreement shall 
bee sayde executorye. 
And that the statute 
</page>
 
<page sig="15v">
of 26. H. 8. cap. 3. 
doth proue, where it 
sayth, that euery vi&#173;
car, person, and such 
lyke &#38;c. before their 
actuall possessyon or 
medling with the pro&#173;
fits of their benefice, 
shall satisfie, content 
&#38;c. or agree to pay to 
the vse of the Queene, 
the first fruits &#38;c. and 
if any such person, vi&#173;
car &#38;c. enter in actu&#173;
al possession &#38;c. this 
agrement is to be vn&#173;
derstoode executory as 
the c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>on vse proues, 
for it is vsed, that hee, 
with one, or ij. <expan type="w+t">with</expan> him 
doe make two or three 
obligations for it, to 
bee payed at certayne 
dayes after. And this 
agreement executory, 
is deuyded in two 
pointes, One is an 
agreement executory, 
which is certeyne at 
the beginning, as is 
sayde laste before of 
the first fruits. 
</page>
 
<page sig="16r">
The other is, where 
the certeinty doth not 
appeare at the first, 
and the partyes are a&#173;
greed, that the thinge 
shalbe perfourmed, or 
payed, vppon the cer&#173;
teinty knowen. As if 
one sell to an other, 
al his wheat in such 
a tasse in his barne vn&#173;
threshed, and it is a&#173;
greed betweene them, 
that he shal pay for e&#173;
uery bushel xij. d. wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
it is threshed cleaned 
&#38; measured.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="aid(n)">&#182; Aide.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="implead(v)">AIde is when tenant 
for terme of life, te&#173;
naunt in dower, te&#173;
nant by curtesie, or te&#173;
nant in taile after pos&#173;
sibilitye of issue ex&#173;
tinct is impleded, then 
for that that they 
haue noe estate but for 
terme of lyfe, they shal 
pray in ayde of him in 
the reuersion, and pro&#173;
ces shall bee made by 
</page>
 
<page sig="16v">
writt against him, to 
come &#38; plede with the 
tenant in the defence 
of the land if he will, 
but it behoueth that 
they agree in the plee, 
for if they vary, <expan type="y+e">the</expan> plee 
of the tenaunt shalbee 
taken &#38; then the ayde 
praier is void, but if he 
come not at the second 
writ, then the tenant 
shall aunswere sole. 
Also tenant for terme 
of yeres, tenant at wil, 
tenant by Elegit, and 
tenant by statute mer&#173;
chaunt, shall haue aide 
of him in the reuersi&#173;
on, and the seruaunt 
and baily of their ma&#173;
ster when they haue 
done any thing law&#173;
fully in the ryght of 
their master, shal haue 
ayde. 
 
Ayde of the Kinge 
is in lyke case as it is 
sayd before of a com&#173;
mon person, and al&#173;
so in many other cases 
</page>
 
<page sig="17r">
where the kinge may 
haue losse, although 
that the tenant be te&#173;
nant in fee simple hee 
shall haue aide, as if 
a rent bee demaunded 
against the kinges te&#173;
naunt whych holdeth 
in chiefe, hee shal haue 
ayde, and so hee shall 
not haue of a common 
person. 
 
Also where a Citie 
or Boroughe hath a 
fee ferme of the kinge, 
and any thing bee de&#173;
maunded against them 
whiche belongeth to 
the fee ferme, they shal 
haue aide for the losse 
of the king. 
 
Also a man shal haue 
ayde of the king in the 
steede of voucher. Also 
the kinges Bailife, 
the collector and pur&#173;
ueyour shall haue aide 
of the kinge, as well 
as the officers of o&#173;
ther persons.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="alien(n)">&#182; Alyen.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="17v">
<xpln lang="en">ALien is he whose 
father &#38; him selfe 
were both borne 
out of the Queenes 
legeance, and if such 
an alien beeing none of 
the Queenes enemies 
but an alyen friende, 
come and dwel here in 
England &#38; haue issue, 
this issue is no alyen 
but English. So if an 
English man go ouer 
the Seas with the 
Queenes licence, and 
there hath issue, this 
issue is no alien.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="alienation(n)">&#182; Alienation.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ALienation is as 
much to say, as to 
make a thing an other 
mans, to alter or put 
the possession of lande 
or other thinge from 
one man to another.</xpln></wordentry>

iury, to say his verdict</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="amendment(n)">&#182; Amendement.</form>
<xpln lang="en">AMendement is, 
when errour is in 
the processe, the Iusti&#173;
ces may amende if af&#173;
ter iudgement. But if 
there be errour in gee&#173;
uing of iudgem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t, they

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="amercement(n)">&#182; Amercement.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="18v">
<xpln lang="en">AMercement most

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="fr">&#182; An, iour, &#38; wast.</form>

<xpln lang="en"><term lang="fr">AN, iour, &#38; wast</term> is a

&#38; the pastures &#38; mea&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="appeal(n)">&#182; Appeale.</form>
<xpln lang="en">APpeal is where one

An Appeale of Mai&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="appendant(n)" lexeme="appurtenant(n)">&#182; Append<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t &#38; appurten<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="apportionment(n)">&#182; Apporcionment.</form>
<xpln lang="en">APporcionment is 
a deuydinge into 
partes of a rent 
(which is deuidable &#38; 
not entier or whole,) 
and for so much as the 
thing for which, or of 
which it was to bee 
paied, is seperated and 
deuided, the rent also 
shalbe deuided, hauing 
respect to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> partes. As 
if a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> haue a r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t ser&#173;
uice issuing out of l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
&#38; he purchaseth parcel 
</page>
 
<page sig="21r">
of the lande, the rent 
shalbe apporcioned ac&#173;
cording to the value of 
the lande. 
 
So if a man hold his 
lande of an other by 
Homage, Fealty, Es&#173;
cuage, and certeine 
rent, if the Lorde of 
whom the lande is 
holden purchase pur&#173;
cell of the lande, the 
rent shalbee apporcio&#173;
ned. 
 
Also if a man lett 
landes and goodes for 
yeares reseruing rent, 
and after a straunger 
recouereth the lande, 
then the rent shalbee 
apporcioned, because 
the goodes are not re&#173;
couered, but remayne. 
And so it is if but 
part of the lande bee 
recouered the rent shal 
bee apporcioned, that 
is to say, deuyded, and 
the lessee shall pay, ha&#173;
uinge respect to that 
whych is recouered, 
and to that whiche 
</page>
 
<page sig="21v">
yet remaines in hys 
handes, according to 
the value. 
 
But a rent charge 
can not be apporcio&#173;
ned, nor thinges that 
are entier. As if one 
hold l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d by seruice to 
pay to his lord yerely 
at such a feast a horse, 
a Hauke, a Rose, a 
Cherry or suche like. 
There if the Lorde 
purchase parcel of the 
lande, this seruice is 
gone altogether, be&#173;
cause a Horse, a 
Hauke, a Rose, a 
Cherry, and such o&#173;
ther, can not bee deui&#173;
ded, seuered, nor 
apporcioned without 
hurt to the whole</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="appropriation(n)">&#182; <emend err="App ropiation">Appropriation</emend>.</form>
<xpln lang="en">APpropryacions 
were when those

mish Religion, &#38; those 
</page>
 
<page sig="22r">
religious persons, as

and suche lyke, had

nye Parsonage to

tayned lycence of 
their holie father the 
Pope, that they them 
selues and their suc&#173;
cessours from thence 
forth should bee par&#173;
sones there, and serue 
the cure. And so at 
the beginnynge ap&#173;
propryations weare 
made onelye to those 
persons spiritual that 
could minister the sa&#173;
craments and say de&#173;
uyne seruice, as Ab&#173;
bottes, Pryours, 
Deanes, and suche 
lyke: After by lyttle 
and little, they were 
enlarged and made to 
other, as namely to 
a Deane and Chap&#173;
ter, whych is a bodye 
corporate, consystinge 
</page>
 
<page sig="22v">
of manie, which bodie 
together, coulde not 
say deuine seruice, and 
what more was to 
Nunnes that were 
Prioresses of some 
Nunrie, which was 
a wicked thinge, in 
so much as they could 
neither minister Sa&#173;
craments nor preach, 
nor say deuine seruyce 
to the Parishioners. 
And al this was vp&#173;
pon pretence of hospi&#173;
talitie, and maynte&#173;
naunce thereof. And 
to supply these defects 
a Vicar was deuysed, 
who should be deputy 
to the Priores, or to 
the Deane and Chap&#173;
ter, and also at the last 
to the saide Abbots &#38; 
others, to say deuine 
seruice, &#38; should haue 
for his labor but a lit&#173;
tle porcion, &#38; they to 
whom the appropria&#173;
tion was made, should 
retaine the great re&#173;
uenues, and they dyd 
</page>
 
<page sig="23r">
nothinge for it, by 
meanes whereof hos&#173;
pitalitye decayed in 
the place where yt 
ought to haue beene 
chiefely mainteyned, 
namely in the paryshe 
where the benefyce 
was, and were the 
profits did growe, 
and so it contynueth 
to this day, to the 
great hynderaunce of 
learning, the impoue&#173;
rishment of the My&#173;
nisterie, and the infa&#173;
mie of the Gospel and 
professors thereof.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="arbitrement(n)">&#182; Arbitrement.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="arrest(n)">&#182; Arrest.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="asset(n)">&#182; Assets.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ASsets is in two 
sortes, the one 
called <term>assets per dis<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cent</term>, the other <term lang="fr">assets en&#173;
ter maines. Assets per

ueth not suffici<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t goodz 
to discharge this obli&#173;
gation, then this land 
shalbe called Assets, 
that is to say, enough 
or sufficient to pay the 
same det, and by that 
meanes the heire shal&#173;
bee charged, as faire 
as the lande so to 
hym dyscended wyll 
</page>
 
<page sig="25r">
stretche: But if hee 
haue alyened before 
the obligatyon be put 
in suite, hee is dys&#173;
charged. 
 
Also when a man 
seised of lands in taile,

wife, alieneth the same

hath in value as much 
l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d in fee simple which 
disc<expan type="e+_">en</expan>deth to his heire, 
who is also heire in 
taile, or heire to the 
woman: Now if the

of his auncestor bring

<term lang="la">sur Cui in vita</term> for the

hee shal bee barred by

rantye and the lande 
so dyscended, which 
is as much in value

and so thereby he hath

and therfore this land 
is called <term lang="fr">Assetes per 
discent</term>. 
</page>
 
<page sig="25v">
<term lang="fr">Assets enter maines</term>, is 
when a man indebted 
as before is sayde, ma&#173;
keth executours and 
leaueth to th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> suffici&#173;
ent to pay, or some c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>&#173;
modity or profit is c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>e 
to th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> in right of their 
testatour, this is said 
assets in their handes.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="assignee(n)">&#182; Assignee.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ASsignee is hee to

nee in deed, &#38; assignee 
in law, assignee in deed

signees or <expan type="w+t">with</expan>out those

teth, or selleth <expan type="y+e">the</expan> same

his assignee in deede. 
</page>
 
<page sig="26r">
Assignee in law is 
euery executor named 
by the testator in hys

to his assignees (as is 
aforesaid) and he ma&#173;

ny other, now the exe&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="attainder(n)">&#182; Attainder.</form>
<xpln lang="en">ATtainder is a con&#173;
uiction of any pers<expan type="o+_">on</expan>,

&#38; this may be ij. waies 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> one vpon apparance,

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="ancient(a)" lexeme="demesne(n)">&#182; Auncien demesne.</form>
<xpln lang="en">AUncien demesne, are

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="avowry(n)">&#182; Auowrie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">AVowrye is where

kinge, and that is cal&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bail(n)">&#182; Baile.</form>
<xpln lang="en">BAile is when a 
man is taken, or 
arrested, for felo&#173;
ny, suspition of felo&#173;
ny, endicted of felo&#173;
ny, or any such case, 
so that he is restray&#173;
ned of his lybertye: 
And beeinge by lawe 
baileable offreth suer&#173;
ty, to those <expan type="y+t">that</expan> haue au&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="28r">
thority to baile hym 
which suerties are 
bounde for him to the 
Queenes vse in a cer&#173;
taine summe of money 
or bodye for bodye, 
that he shall appeare 
beefore the Iustices 
of Gaole deliuery at 
the next sessions &#38;c. 
Then vpon the bonds 
of these suerties, as 
is aforesaide, he is 
bailed, that is to say, 
sett at libertye, vntil 
the day appointed for 
his apparance.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bailment(n)">&#182; Bailement</form>

<expan type="y+e">the</expan> baily, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is to say of 
him to wh<expan type="o+_">om</expan> it is dely&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bailiff(n)">&#182; Bailife.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="reeve(n)">BAilife is an offi&#173;

and hath aucthoritye. 
to paye quitrents is&#173;
suing out of the man&#173;

not then knowne a&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="thief(n)" lexeme="back-berend(a)">&#182; Bakberinde theefe.</form>
<xpln lang="en">BAkberind Theefe, 
is a theefe that is

that found vppon him 
(being followed <expan type="w+t">with</expan> the

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bargain(n)" lexeme="sale(n)">&#182; Bargaine &#38; sale.</form>
<xpln lang="en">BArgaine and sale, 
is when a recom&#173;
pence is geuen by 
both the partyes to 
the bargayne. As if 
one bargaine and sell 
his land to another for 
money. Here the lande 
is a recompence to him 
for the money, and the 
mony is a recompence 
to the other for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> land, 
and this is a good con&#173;
tract and bargaine, and 
fee simple passeth, not&#173;
withstandyng he doth 
not saye, to haue and 
to holde the lande to 
him and to his heires. 
</page>
 
<page sig="29v">
And by such a bargain 
and sale, landes maye 
passe without lyuerye 
of seisin, if the bargain 
and sale be by deed in&#173;
dented, sealed, and in&#173;
rolled, either in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
ty where the land ly&#173;
eth, or in one of the 
Queenes courtes of 
Records at Westmin&#173;
ster, <expan type="w+t">with</expan>in vj. moneths 
next after the date of 
the same writinge en&#173;
dented according to <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
statute in that behalfe 
made in the 27. yeare 
of H.8.ca.16.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="bastard(n)">&#182; Bastarde.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="child(n)" lexeme="people(n)">BAstard is he that is

</page>
 
<page sig="30r">
not maried so that his 
father is not knowen 
by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> order of the law, 
&#38; therefore he is called

But by the law spiri&#173;
tual if one get a childe 
vpon a woman which 
childe is borne out of

trey and not by the 
Byshoppe. But ge&#173;
nerall bastardye allea&#173;

the certificat of the 
Bishop. 
 
And if a woman be

&#38; she taketh an other

</page>
 
<page sig="30v">
the firste husbande. 
But if shee were pri&#173;

<expan type="y+e">the</expan> sec<expan type="o+_">on</expan>d husb<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d, but en&#173;

Also if a man take

with childe by an o&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="battle(n)">&#182; Battaile.</form>
<xpln lang="en">BAttaile is an aun&#173;

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="burglary(n)">&#182; Burglarie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">BVrglarie is when 
one breaketh and 
entreth into the house 
of another in the night 
with felonious intent 
to robbe or kill, or to 
do some other felonie, 
in whiche cases al&#173;
though he carie away 
nothing, yet is it felo&#173;
nie, for which he shal 
suffer death. Other&#173;
wise it is if it be in the 
day time, or that hee 
break the house in the 
night, and enter not 
therein at that time. 
</page>
 
<page sig="34r">
But if a seruant wil 
conspire wyth other 
men to robbe his Ma&#173;
ster, and to that intent 
he openeth hys Ma&#173;
sters doores or wyn&#173;
dowes in the nyght 
for them, and they 
come into the house 
by that way, thys 
is Burglarye in the 
straungers, and the 
seruant is a theefe but 
no burglar. And this 
was the opinion of 
the Right worshipful 
Syr Roger Manwoode 
Knight, most woor&#173;
thy Lord chiefe Ba&#173;
ron of the Eschequer, 
at the Quarter Ses&#173;
sions holden in Can&#173;
terburie in Ianuarie 
last 1579. 21. Eli&#173;
zabeth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="challenge(n)">&#182; Challenge.</form>
<xpln lang="en">CHallenge, is where 
Iurours appeare 
to trie an issue, then 
if anye, of the par&#173;
ties suppose that they 
are not indyfferent, 
</page>
 
<page sig="35r">
they may there chal&#173;
lenge and refuse them. 
There be diuers chal&#173;
lenges, one is chal&#173;
lenge to the array, the 
other to the polles. 
Challenge to tharray 
is when the panell is 
fauourably made by 
the Sherife or other 
Officer. Challenge by 
the polles, are some 
principal, and some by 
cause as they call it. 
Principall is when 
one of the Iurors is 
the sonne, brother, or 
cousin, to the plaintyfe 
or defendant or tenant 
to him, or that he hath 
espoused the daughter 
of the plaintife, &#38; for 
those causes hee shalbe 
withdrawen. 
 
Also in a plee of the 
death of a man, and in 
euery other action real 
&#38; in actions personal, 
if the debt or damages 
amount to xl. Markes 
it is a good challenge, 
that he cannot disp<expan type="e+_">en</expan>de 
</page>
 
<page sig="35v">
xl. s. by the yeare of 
freeholde. 
 
Challenge by cause, 
is where the partye 
doth alleage a matter 
which is no principall 
challenge, as that the 
sonne of one of the iu&#173;
rors hath espoused the 
daughter of the plain&#173;
tife, &#38; then he doth c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>&#173;
clude, &#38; therefore he is 
fauorable, whych shal 
be tried by others of 
thenquest, whether he 
be fauorable or indif&#173;
ferent, and if they say 
that is fauorable &#38; 
not indifferent, th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> he 
shalbee drawen out, 
otherwise he shalbee 
sworne. Also a Felon 
that is arraigned may 
challenge xx. Iurours 
peremptorie without 
any cause, and that is 
in fauor of life: and as 
many as he will wyth 
cause, but th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> it shal be 
tried if for such cause 
he be indiffer<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t or not.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="champertor(n)">&#182; Champertours.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="36r">
<xpln lang="en">CHampertors be they

or others procurem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="charge(n)">&#182; Charge.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="rentcharge(n)">CHarge is where a

But if one graunt a

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="chattel(n)">&#182; Chattels.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="chimin(n)">&#182; Chimin.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="thing(n)"  lexeme="action(n)">&#182; Thinge in action.</form>

some dutye due to him 
as an actyon of debt 
vpon an oblagation, 
annuity, rent, couen<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t 
warde, goodes, trespas 
or such like. And bee&#173;
cause they are thinges 
whereof a man is not 
possessed, but for reco&#173;
uery of them is driu<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
to his actyon, they are 
called things in acti<expan type="o+_">on</expan>, 
&#38; those things in acti&#173;
on that are certeine, 
the Queene may gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t 
and the grauntee may 
vse an action for them 
in his owne name on&#173;
ly. But a comm<expan type="o+_">on</expan> per&#173;
son can not graunte 
hys thinge in actyon, 
nor the Queene her 
selfe can not graunt 
her thinge in actyon 
which is vncerteyne, 
as trespas &#38; such like.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="circuit(n)" lexeme="action(n)">&#182; Circuit of action.</form>
<xpln lang="en">CIrcuite of acti<expan type="o+_">on</expan> is 
when an actyon is 
</page>
 
<page sig="38r">
rightly brought for a 
dutye: but yet about <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
bushe as it were, for <emend err="y{e}"><expan type="y+t">that</expan></emend>
it might aswel bene 
otherwise aunswered 
and determined, and <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
suite saued, and bee&#173;
cause that the same ac&#173;
tion was more then 
needefull, it is called 
circuite of actyon. As 
if a man graunt a rent 
charge of x. li. out of 
his mannour of Dale, 
and after the graun&#173;
tee disseise the graun&#173;
tour of the same Ma&#173;
nour of Dale, and hee 
bring<expan type="e+_">en</expan>th an assise and 
recouereth the lande, 
and xx. li. dammages, 
which xx. li. beeynge 
paied, the grauntee of 
the rent sueth his ac&#173;
tyon for x. li. of his 
rent due duringe the 
time of the disseison, 
which if no disseisine 
had ben, he must haue 
had. This is called cir<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cuit of acti<expan type="o+_">on</expan> because it 
might haue b<expan type="e+_">en</expan> shortly 
</page>
 
<page sig="38v">
aunswered, for where 
as the gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>tor should 
receiue xx. li. damages, 
and pay x. li. rent, hee 
might haue receyued 
but the x. li. onely for 
the damages, and the 
grauntee myght haue 
cut of and kept backe 
the other x. li. in hys 
handes by way of de&#173;
tainer for his rent, and 
so there by, mought 
haue saued his action.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="claim(n)">&#182; Clayme.</form>
<xpln lang="en">CLaime is a chal&#173;
lenge vp any man 
of the property or ow&#173;
nershippe of a thinge 
which he hath not in 
possession, but which 
is withholden from 
him wrongfully.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="clergy(n)">&#182; Clergie.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="book(n)" lexeme="ordinary(n)">CLergie is an aunci&#173;
ent lybertie of the 
Popish church, which 
hath also ben c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>firmed 
</page>
 
<page sig="39r">
with vs in dyuers 
Parliamentes. And it 
is when a Priest, or 
one within holie Or&#173;
ders (as they terme 
it) or any other what 
soeuer, in whom is no 
impediment or impos&#173;
sibilitie to be a Priest, 
is arraigned of felonie 
or such like before a 
temporall Iudge &#38;c. 
and the prisoner pray&#173;
eth his Clergie, that 
is to say, to haue hys 
booke, whych is as 
much as if he desyred 
to bee dismissed from 
the Temporal Iudge, 
and to bee deliuered 
to the Ordinarie to 
purge hymselfe of the 
same offence. Thys 
priuiledge at the first 
was not so generall, 
in respect of the par&#173;
ties that should take 
benefite thereby, as 
it afterwarde became 
to bee, for at the be&#173;
ginnyng, beeynge a 
Popishe inuention, 
</page>
 
<page sig="39v">
the Patrons thereof 
were very parcial, and 
woulde not that any 
should reape commodi&#173;
tie thereby, but their 
popish Priestes onely 
and such as were with 
in Orders, as is afore 
saide. And this arose 
amonge them, partly 
through their greate 
pryde, disdaining to be 
vnder the obedience of 
their naturall kinges 
and temporal correcti&#173;
on, and partly of po&#173;
licie, for shame lest the 
lewde maners of their 
spiritualitie, shoulde 
come to the open view 
and examynation of 
the laitie, (as they dis&#173;
tinguish them) and no 
meruail at al, for with 
in a few of the fyrst 
yeares of king Henry 
the seconds raigne, the 
Clergy of the Realme 
had committed aboue 
one hundrede seuerall 
murders vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan> his sub&#173;
iectes, as the king was 
</page>
 
<page sig="40r">
certeinely informed, 
besides many robbe&#173;
ries and other outra&#173;
ges, for remedie where 
of, order was ta&#173;
ken by the kinge, his 
Nobilitie, and wyth 
much a doe the Cler&#173;
gie consented thereto, 
that if any clerke from 
thence forth commit&#173;
ted Felony or Trea&#173;
son, he should first be 
degraded, and after&#173;
warde deliuered to the 
lay power, there to 
receiue as to his of&#173;
fence belonged &#38;c. at 
the last in fauour of 
life, (a thinge to bee 
shewed indifferentlye 
towards al mankind) 
and for the loue of 
learning, it was gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;
ted to all men that 
coulde reade, though 
they weare neyther 
Priestes, nor within 
orders. And since in 
Parliam<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t made vpon 
good considerations, it 
hath been restrayned 
</page>
 
<page sig="40v">
and taken away in di&#173;
uers cases, as in wil&#173;
full murder, burglary, 
and such others.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="clerk(n)" lexeme="attaint(a)" lexeme="convict(a)">&#182; Clerke attaint, 
Clerke conuict.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="purgation(n)">CLerkes are in two

Clerke attaint is hee

of the felonie, and hath 
his clergy to him gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="colour(n)">&#182; Colour.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COlour, is a fayned

</page>
 
<page sig="41r">
defendaunt or tenant

ful to the comm<expan type="o+_">on</expan> peo&#173;

the reuersion to A. 
the demaundment, and 
</page>
 
<page sig="41v">
after C. the tenaunt 
for terme of lyfe died,

the demaundant clay&#173;

gainst wh<expan type="o+_">om</expan>A. for that 
entre bringes this as&#173;

Also in an action of

<page sig="42r">

tife bringeth an action; 
this is a good colour, 
and a good plea.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="colour(n)" lexeme="office(n)">&#182; Colour of office.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COlour of office, is

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="collusion(n)">&#182; Collusion.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COllusion is where

<page sig="43r">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="common law(n)">&#182; Commen law.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="civil law(n)" lexeme="admiral(n)" lexeme="King's Bench(n)" lexeme="base court(n)" lexeme="court-baron(n)" lexeme="piepowder(n)" lexeme="pleadable(a)">COmmon law, is for 
the most part taken 
3. waies, first for the 
lawes of this Realme 
simply without any o&#173;
ther lawe, as custo&#173;
mary lawe, Ciuil law,

whatsoeuer els lawe 
ioyned vnto it, as wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
it is desputed in our

what ought of right 
to bee determyned by 
the common lawe, 
and what by the spiri&#173;
tuall lawe, or Admi&#173;
rales Court, or such 
lyke. 
 
Secondly it is taken 
for the kings courtes, 
as the kinges Bench, 
or common place, one&#173;
lye to shewe a diffe&#173;
rence betweene them 
and the base courtes, 
courtes barons, coun&#173;
tie courtes, pipow&#173;
ders, and such like, as

</page>
 
<page sig="43v">
is remoued out of a<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;

the lande is franke fee 
and pleadable at the 
c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon law, that is to 
say in the kings court 
and not in auncien de&#173;
mesne, or in any other 
base court. 
 
Thirdly and moste 
vsually by the c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon 
law is vnderstood, such 
lawes as were gene&#173;
rally taken and holden 
for lawe before anye 
statute was made to 
alter the same: as for 
example. Tenaunt for 
lyfe, not for yeares, 
were not to be puny&#173;
shed for doing wast at 
the common lawe, tyl 
the statute of Glouces&#173;
ter. cap 5. was made 
which doth geeue an 
action of wast against 
them: But tenant by 
the curtesie, and te&#173;
naunt in dower, were 
punyshable of waste, 
at the common lawe, 
that is to saye, by 
</page>
 
<page sig="44r">
the vsuall, and c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon 
receiued lawes of the 
realme, before the said 
statute of Glocester 
was made.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="common(n)">&#182; Common.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="common(n)" lexeme="gross(n)" lexeme="common appendant(n)" lexeme="appurtenant(n)" lexeme="neighborhood(n)" lexeme="comprest(v)">COmon is the right 
that a man hath to 
put his beastes to pas<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ture, or to vse &#38; occupy

his owne. 
 
And note <expan type="y+t">that</expan> there be

c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon appendant, c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>&#173;

Common in grosse is 
where I by my deede 
gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>t to another that 
he shall haue common 
in my lande 
 
Common appendant 
is where a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> is seised 
of certaine land, to the 
which he hath c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon 
in anothers grounde,

</page>

And alwayes this 
c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon in by prescrip&#173;

ryght, and it is ap&#173;

Common appurte&#173;

And such c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon may

</page>
 
<page sig="45r">
Common by cause of

But the one may

others ground, for soe

may distraine th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> d<expan type="a+_">am</expan>&#173;

pas, but they may put

And the inhabit<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ts of 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> one town ought not

</page>
 
<page sig="45v">
towne, for otherwise

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="condition(n)">&#182; Condytion.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="condition(n)" lexeme="actual(a)" lexeme="expressed(a)" lexeme="deed(n)" lexeme="law(n)" lexeme="precedent(a)" lexeme="subsequent(a)" lexeme="bridle(n)">COndition is a res&#173;
traint or bridle <expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;
nexed, and ioyned 
to a thinge, so that by 
the not performance 
or not doinge thereof, 
the party to the condi<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cion shall receiue pre&#173;
iudice and lose, &#38; by

dooynge of the s<expan type="a+_">am</expan>e c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>&#173;
modity &#38; aduantage. 
 
And all condityons 
are either condityons 
actuall and expressed, 
which he called con&#173;
ditions in deede, or els 
they bee conditions 
implyed or couert &#38; 
not expressed, which 
are called conditions 
in law. 
 
Also al condytions 
are either conditions 
</page>
 
<page sig="46r">
precedent and goinge 
before the estate &#38; are 
executed or els subse&#173;
quent, and following 
after the estate and 
executorie. 
 
The condition pre&#173;
cedent, doth gaine and 
gett the thinge or es&#173;
tate made vpon con&#173;
dition by the perfor&#173;
mance of the same. 
 
The condition sub&#173;
sequent, doth keepe &#38; 
continue the thinge 
or estate made vppon 
condition by the per&#173;
formance of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> same 
 
Actuall and expres&#173;
sed condition, which 
is called a condition 
in deede: is a condity&#173;
on knitt and annexed 
by expresse wordes to 
the feoffement, leas, 
or graunt, either in 
writinge or without 
writinge, as it Fen&#173;
feoffe a man in landes 
reseruing r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t to be pai&#173;

conditi<expan type="o+_">on</expan> <expan type="y+t">that</expan> if <expan type="y+t">that</expan> feofee 
</page>
 
<page sig="46v">
faile of payment at the

Condition implyed

perteyninge to his of&#173;
fice by himselfe or his 
sufficyent deputye, 
then it shall bee law&#173;
full to the grauntour 
to enter and discharge 
him of his office. Con&#173;
dition precedent and 
goinge before is when 
a leas is made to one 
for life vpon condition 
</page>
 
<page sig="47r">
that if the lessee for 
life, will paie to the 
lessor xx.li. at such a 
day, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> he shal haue 
fee simple: here <expan type="y+t">that</expan> con&#173;
dicion preceeds &#38; go&#173;
eth beefore the estate 
in fee simple, and vpp<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
the performance of <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
condycion, doth get

ple. Condition subse&#173;
quent and followinge 
after, is when one

simple, vpon condity&#173;
on, that <expan type="y+e">the</expan> grauntee

conditi<expan type="o+_">on</expan> is subsequ<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
&#38; following the estate 
in fee simple, and vpon 
the performance there 
of, doth keepe and con&#173;
tinue the estate.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="good(n)" lexeme="confiscate(a)">&#182; Confiscate goods.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="mainour(n)">COnfiscate goods 
are goods to which 
</page>
 
<page sig="47v">
the lawe intitleth the 
Queene, when they

indited that he feloni&#173;
ously stole the goods of 
I.S. where in truith 
they are hys owne 
goodes, and they are 
brought into the court 
against him as a mai&#173;
neur, &#38; then is dema<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
ded, what he sayth to 
those goods, and he de&#173;
nieth them, nowe by 
this denying of them, 
hee shall loose those 
goods, although that 
afterwarde he be ac&#173;
quited of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> felony, and 
soe in other lyke ca&#173;
ses.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="contract(n)">&#182; Contracte.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="quid pro quo(n)">COntracte is a bar&#173;
gaine or couenaunt 
betweene two parties, 
where one thinge is 
geeuen for an other 
which is called <term lang="la">quid 
pro quo</term>, as if I sell 
</page>
 
<page sig="48r">
my horse for money, or 
if I couenant to make 
you a lease of my man&#173;
nor of Dale in consi&#173;
deration of xx.li. that 
you shal giue me, these 
are good contracts be&#173;
cause there is one th<expan type="i+_">in</expan>g 
for an other, But if 
a man make promyse 
to mee that I shall 
haue twentye shyl&#173;
linges, and that hee 
wil be debtour to mee 
thereof, and after I 
aske <emend err="the the">the</emend> xx.s. and 
hee wil not deliuer it, 
yet I shal neuer haue 
any action to recouer 
this xx.s. for that, that 
this promise was no 
contracte but a bare 
<emend err="promys e">promyse</emend>, and <term lang="la">ex nu&#173;
do practo non oritur ac&#173;
tio</term>: but if any thinge 
were geuen for the xx. 
shillinges though it 
were not but to the 
value of a peny, then 
it had ben a good con&#173;
tracte.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="48v">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="conusance(n)">&#182; Conusance.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COnusance of plee, 
is a priuiledge that 
a citie or Towne 
hath of the kinges 
graunt to holde plee 
of al contractes, and 
of landes within the 
precinct of the fran&#173;
chise: and when anye 
man is impleaded for 
any such thinge in <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
Court at <emend err="Westmis-">Westm<expan type="i+_">in</expan>s&#173;</emend>
ter: the Maior and 
bailifes of such fraun&#173;
ches or theyr attur&#173;
ney may aske conu&#173;
sance of the plee, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is 
to say, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> <expan type="y+e">the</expan> plee &#38; <expan type="y+e">the</expan> <emend err="mat">mat&#173;</emend>
ter shal be pleded &#38; de&#173;
termined before th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>. 
 
But if the Court 
at Westeminster bee 
lawefullye seised of 
the Plee, beefore 
Conusaunce bee de&#173;
maunded, then they 
shall not haue Co&#173;
nusance for that suit, 
because they haue neg&#173;
lig<expan type="e+_">en</expan>tly surcessed their 
</page>
 
<page sig="49r">
time of demaunde, but 
this shal be no barre to 
them to haue <emend err="conusace">conus<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce</emend>
in an other action, for 
they may demaunde 
conusance in one acti&#173;
on, and omit it in an 
other action at theyr 
pleasure. 
 
And note that conu&#173;
sance lyeth not in pre&#173;
scription, but it beho&#173;
ueth to shew <expan type="y+e">the</expan> kinges 
letters.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="corody(n)">&#182; Corodie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COrodie, was a rea&#173;
sonable allowance 
of Meat, bread, drink, 
money, clothing, lod&#173;
ging, and such like sus&#173;
tenance, which of com&#173;
mon right euery foun&#173;
dor of Abbeies, Prio&#173;
ries, Nunries, &#38; other 
houses of religion, had 
in the same house, wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
any were standing, for 
his father, brother, co&#173;
sine, or other man that 
hee woulde appoynt 
</page>
 
<page sig="49v">
should take it, yf it 
were a house of Mon&#173;
kes, and if hee were 
foundor of a house of 
Nunnes or women, 
then the same for hys 
mother, sister, cosin, or 
other woman that he 
would direct thither, 
and alwaies this was 
prouided for, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> he that 
had corodie in a house 
of Monkes, might not 
send a woman to take 
it. Nor where corodie 
was due in a Nunrie, 
there it was not law&#173;
full to appoint a man 
to receiue <expan type="y+e">the</expan> same, for 
in both cases, such pre&#173;
s<expan type="e+_">en</expan>tacion was to be re&#173;
iected. And this Co&#173;
rodie was due as well 
to a common person <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
was fo<expan type="u+_">un</expan>dor, as where 
the king him self was 
foundor. But where <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
house was holden in 
frankalmoigne, there 
the tenure it selfe was 
a dyscharge of Co&#173;
rodye agaynste all 
</page>
 
<page sig="50r">
men. Except it were 
afterward charged vo&#173;
lantarily, as wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> the 
king would sende hys 
writ to the Abbey for 
a Corodie for such a 
one whom they admit, 
there the house should 
bee charged for euer, 
whether <expan type="y+e">the</expan> king were 
foundor or not.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="crowner(n)">&#182; Crowner.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="coroner(n)" lexeme="conservator(n)">CRowner is an aun&#173;

</page>
 
<page sig="50v">
the office is not had in

careful as they should 
bee in theyr electyon: 
and therefore, it is 
nowe almost come a&#173;
gaine into that plight 
that it was in Kynge 
Edwarde the firstes 
daies, when this sta&#173;
tute followinge was

&#38;c. And although the

</page>
 
<page sig="51r">

serued: yet at the least

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="corporation(n)">&#182; Corporatyon.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COrporation ys a 
permanent thinge 
that may haue suc&#173;
cession: And is an 
assembly and ioyning 
together of many into 
one felowshippe, bro&#173;
therhoode and minde, 
whereof one is hedde 
and chiefe, the rest are 
the bodye: and thys

</page>
 
<page sig="51v">
And of Corporaty&#173;
ons, some are called 
spirituall, and some

some are corporations 
of deade personnes in 
lawe, and some other 
wyse, and some are 
by the aucthorytye of 
the Kynge onelye, 
and some haue beene 
of a myxt authorytye, 
and of those that are 
Temporall, some are 
by the aucthorytye of 
the Kynge also, and 
some by the Com&#173;
mon lawe of the 
Realme. 
 
Corporation spiri&#173;
tual and of dead per&#173;
sons in lawe, is where 
the corporatyon con&#173;
sisteth of an Abbot &#38; 
Couent, and these had 
beginning of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> king 
and the man of Rome 
when hee had to doe 
here. 
 
Corporati<expan type="o+_">on</expan> spiritual 
&#38; of able pers<expan type="o+_">on</expan>z in law

<page sig="52r">
is where the corpora&#173;

and this <emend err="corporaton">corporation</emend>, 
had beginninge of the 
Kinge onely. 
 
Corporation Tem&#173;
poral by the Kinge is 
where there is a ma&#173;

Corporation tem&#173;
porall by aucthoritye 
of the common lawe 
is the assemblye in <emend err="par">par&#173;</emend>

sisteth of the Queene 
the hedde of the Cor&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="corruption(n)" lexeme="blood(n)">&#182; Coruption of blood.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="52v">
<xpln lang="en">COrruption of blood

cannot bee heires to

they claim by their fa&#173;

out aucthority of par&#173;
liament.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="covin(n)">&#182; Couin.</form>
<xpln lang="en">COuin is a secrete

in the hartes of two 
or more, to the preiu&#173;
dyce of any other. As 
if a tenaunt for terme 
of life, will secretly 
conspire with an o&#173;

shall recouer agaynst 
the tenaunt for lyfe, 
the lande which hee 
holdeth &#38;c. in preiu&#173;
dice of hym in the re&#173;
uersion.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="counterplea(n)">&#182; Counterplee.</form>
<xpln lang="en">Counterplee, ys

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="Cinque Ports(pn)">&#182; Cinque Portes.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="Hastings(pn)" lexeme="Dover(pn)" lexeme="Romney(pn)" lexeme="Hithe(pn)" lexeme="Sandwich(pn)" lexeme="Court of Shipway(pn)" lexeme="Pevensea(pn)" lexeme="Bulverhythe(pn)" lexeme="Petit Iham(pn)" lexeme="Bekesbourne(pn)" lexeme="Greneth(pn)" lexeme="Rye(pn)" lexeme="Winchelsea(pn)" lexeme="Seaford(pn)" lexeme="Hideny(pn)" lexeme="Northeye(pn)" lexeme="Woleworchety(pn)"  lexeme="Lydd(pn)" lexeme="Old Romney(pn)" lexeme="Fordwich(pn)" lexeme="Sarre(pn)" lexeme="Stonor(pn)" lexeme="Deal(pn)" lexeme="Faversham(pn)" lexeme="Folkestone(pn)" lexeme="Broomhill(pn)" lexeme="Orwaldstone(pn)" lexeme="Dengemarsh(pn)" lexeme="Margate(pn)" lexeme="Reculver(pn)" lexeme="grommet(n)">CInque Portes, bee

since, many liberties,

Douer, Sandwicus,

said court ought not 
to be holden from the 
feast of the natiuity of 
saint Mary, vntil the 
feast of saint Andrew, 
because of the martes 
of Germany. 
 
Also when the Ba&#173;
rons of the Cinque 
ports are in the kings 
seruice vpon the Sea, 
or at the kings sum&#173;
mons, or at the kings 
commaundement. 
 
Furthermore, it 
ought not to be holden 
but one day. 
 
And one Essoine on&#173;
lie lyeth in the afore&#173;
sayde Court in euery 
plea. 
 
Of sute no Essoine on&#173;
lie lyeth in the afore&#173;
sayde Court in euery 
plea. 
 
Of sute no Essoine 
lieth, as is before said, 
and therefore if the 
maior, who because 
of sickenesse or other 
sodeyne infirmytye 
cannot come thither, 
</page>
 
<page sig="58v">
an other may at that 
daye keepe his place, 
so notwithstandinge 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> returne be made by 
his bailife. 
 
Nor others princi&#173;
pally ought to be char<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ged of any iudgement 
giuen in the same 
court but those names 
who by the Baylifes 
there haue beene re&#173;
turned. 
 
Bisides all thys, 
prouision of Shippes 
and men, as is afore&#173;
saide: I haue seene in 
an other record (short&#173;
lye written ) that e&#173;
uerye Shippe ought 
to haue a boye, which 
there is called Gro&#173;
met: so that in su<expan type="u+_">um</expan>me 
the Cinque ports are 
charged with 57 ships 
1197. men , and fif&#173;
tye seuen boies , or 
Gromets.</xpln>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="half-blood(n)">&#182; Halfe bloode.</form>

not be heire to other,

cent, must bee of the 
whole blodde to him 
from whome he clay&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="devise(n)">&#182; Deuise.</form>
<xpln lang="en">DEuise is where a

ment geeueth or

ther after his decease. 
 
And where such de&#173;

&#38;c. And at that tyme,

I will therefore sett

do carie by the wise

</page>

If one wil that his

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="descent(n)">&#182; Discent.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="lineal(a)" lexeme="collateral(a)">DIscent is in two 
sortes, either lini&#173;

Liniall discent, is

graundfathers bro&#173;

warde.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="disclaimer(n)">&#182; Disclaimer.

<page sig="68v">
<xpln lang="en">DIsclaymer, is

distrayneth hys ten<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t, 
&#38; he sueth a Repleuin 
&#38; the Lord auoweth <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
taking by reason that 
he holdeth of hym, if 
the tenant say that hee 
disclaymeth to hold of 
him, thys is called a 
disclaimer, &#38; if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Lord 
therupon bring a writ 
of right sur disclaimer 
&#38; it be founde agaynst 
the tenaunt, hee shall 
lose the lande.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="tithe(n)">&#182; Tythes.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="predial(a)" lexeme="personal(a)" lexeme="mixed(a)">TIthes are in three 
sortes deuyded, to 
witte, Predyal tithes 
Parsonal tithes, and 
Mixt tithes. 
 
Prediall tithes, are 
tithes that be paied of 
thinges that come of 
the grounde onely, 
as Corne, Haye, 
fruites of trees, and 
such like. 
 
Parsonal tithes, are 
</page>
 
<page sig="69r">
tithes that bee payed 
of such profits as come 
by the labour and in&#173;
dustrie of a mans per&#173;
son, as by buying, sel&#173;
ling, gaines, of mar&#173;
chandise, and of handy 
craftes men, labou&#173;
rers, &#38; such as worke 
for hyer, as Carpen&#173;
ters, Masons, and 
such like. 
 
Mixt tithes are the 
tythes of Calues, 
Lambes, Pigges, and 
such like, that encrease 
partly of the grounde 
that they be fed vpon, 
and partly of the kee&#173;
ping, industrie, &#38; dili&#173;
gence of the owner.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="disparagement(n)">&#182; Disperagement. 
*DIsperagement, </form><xpln lang="en">is 
a shame, disgrace, 
or villany done by the 
Gardein in Chiualry, 
to his ward in chiual&#173;
rie, (which in olde 
time was as much to 
say as a Gentleman) 
</page>
 
<page sig="69v">
being within age, by 
reason of maryage. As 
when the Gardeine 
doth marrie his ward 
within the age of xiiij. 
yeares, and within 
such time that he can&#173;
not consent to marry&#173;
age, to a bondwoman, 
or to the daughter of 
one that dwelt in a 
borough, (which is to 
bee vnderstoode suche 
whose fathers professe 
handycraftes, &#38; those 
baser artes of buying &#38; 
sellinge to gett theyr 
lyuing by) or to one 
that hath but one foote 
or one hand, or is lame 
or deformed, or hath 
some horrible disease, 
as the leprosie, French 
pockes, falling sicknes 
or such like, or marieth 
him to a wom<expan type="a+_">an</expan> that is 
past child bearing, and 
diuers such other: then 
vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan> <expan type="y+e">the</expan> complaint made 
by the friendes of such 
heire, <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Lord or garden 
shal lose <expan type="y+e">the</expan> wardship, &#38; 
</page>
 
<page sig="70r">
the profits during the 
nonage of the heire, 
for the shame done vn&#173;
to hym.</xpln></wordentry>

<xpln lang="en">DIsseisin is when a

any lands or tenem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts

out <expan type="y+t">that</expan> hath the freehold</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="disseisin(n)">&#182; Disseisin vpon disseisin.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="disseisor(n)" lexeme="disseisee(n)">&#182; Disseisour and disseisee.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="distress(n)">&#182; Distresse. 
</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="70v">
<xpln lang="en">DIstres is the thing 
which is taken and 
distreined vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan> any l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d 
for r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t behind, or other 
duitie, or for hurt don, 
although <expan type="y+t">that</expan> the proper&#173;

to a str<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ger, but if they 
be beastes that belong 
to a straunger, it beho&#173;
ueth that they be le&#173;
uant and couchant vp

certain space that they 
haue them selfe well 
rested there, or els they 
bee not distreynable. 
And if one distrain for 
rent or other thinge 
without cause lawful, 
then the party greeued 
shall haue a Repleuin 
vpon suertie found to 
pursue hys action, and 
shall haue <expan type="y+e">the</expan> distres to 
him deliuered againe. 
 
But there be dyuers

distrainable, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is to say 
an other mans gowne 
</page>
 
<page sig="71r">
in the house of a Tai&#173;

that they bee common 
artificers, and that the 
common presumption

belong not to the Ar&#173;
tificer, but to other 
persons which put th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>
there to be wrought. 
 
Also vittaile is not 
distraynable, nor corne 
in sheeues, but if they 
be in a cart, for that, 
that a distres ought to 
be alway of such thin&#173;
ges whereof the she&#173;
rife may make Reple&#173;
uin, and deliuer againe 
in as good case as it 
was at the time of the 
takinge. 
 
A man may distraine 
for homage, and fealty 
and escuage, and other 
seruices, &#38; for fines &#38; 
amerciamentes whych 
be assessed in a Leete, 
but not in a Court 
baron. And also for 
</page>
 
<page sig="71v">
dammage fesant, that 
is to say, when he fin&#173;
deth <expan type="y+e">the</expan> beasts or goods 
of any other, doinge 
hurt or cumbring his 
grounde. But a man 
may not distrain for a&#173;
ny r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t or thing due for 
any l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d, but vpon the 
same l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is charged 
therewith, but in case 
where I come to dis&#173;
trein, &#38; <expan type="y+e">the</expan> other seeing 
my purpose, chaseth <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
beasts, or beareth the

<expan type="y+t">that</expan> I shall not take it

wel pursu, &#38; if I take

as vpon the land char&#173;
ged to whom soeuer 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> <expan type="p_,">pro</expan>perty of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> goods be 
Also for fines &#38; amer&#173;
ceam<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts which be as&#173;
sessed in a leet, one may 
alway take <expan type="y+e">the</expan> goods of 
h<expan type="i+_">im</expan> <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is so amerced, in 
</page>
 
<page sig="72r">
<emend err="wose">whose</emend> grounde soeuer 
they bee with in the 
Iurisdiction of the

And when one hath

hee (if the distresse

and then if the beast

But if hee bringe

that the Sherife may

</page>
 
<page sig="72v">

Withernam, directed

hath made deliuer<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ce 
of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> first distres. Also

&#38; beat downe <expan type="y+e">the</expan> castel. 
As it appeareth by <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
Stature West.I.cap. 
17. Therefore looke

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="divorce(n)">&#182; Diuorce.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="double plea(n)">&#182; Double plea.</form>
<xpln lang="en">Double plee, is where

comprehended, and e&#173;
uery one by himselfe 
is a sufficyent barre or 
aunswere to the acty&#173;
on, then such a double 
plee shall not be ad&#173;
mitted for a plee ex&#173;
cept one depende vpon 
an other, and in such 
case if hee may not 
haue the last plee with 
out the first plee then 
</page>
 
<page sig="73v">
such a double plee shall 
be wel suffered.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="right(n)">&#182; Right. </form>
<xpln lang="en">RIght is where one

ther wr<expan type="o+_">on</expan>fully, as by 
disseisine, or puttinge 
out, or such like. And 
the challenge or claime 
that hee hath, who 
should haue the thing 
is called right.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="right(n)" lexeme="entry(n)">&#182; Right of entrie. </form>
<xpln lang="en">RIght of entrie, is 
when one seised of

disseysed: Nowe the

may so do wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> he wil: 
or els hee may haue a
