<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="privy(n)" lexeme="privity(n)">&#182; Priuie or Priuitie, and 
Priuies.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="testator(n)" lexeme="estate(n)" lexeme="deed(n)" lexeme="law(n)" lexeme="privy(n)">PRiuie, or priuity is 
wher a lease is made 
to holde at will, for 
yeres, for life, or a fef&#173;
fement in fee, &#38; in dy&#173;
uers other cases, now 
because of thys that 
hath passed betweene 
these parties, they are 
called priuies, in res&#173;
pect of straungers be&#173;
twene whom no such 
dealings, or conueian&#173;
ces hath ben. 
 
Also if there be lord 
and tenaunt, and the 
tenaunt holdeth of the 
Lorde by certeyn ser&#173;
uyce, there is a pri&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="160r">
uitie betwene th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> be&#173;
cause of the tenure, &#38; if 
the tenaunt bee dissei&#173;
sed by a stra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ger, there 
is no priuity betwene 
the disseisor &#38; the lord, 
but the priuity stil re&#173;
maineth betwene the 
Lord and the tenaunt 
that is disseysed, and 
the Lord shall auowe 
vpon him, for that hee 
is his tenant in right 
and in the iudgement 
of the lawe, Priuies 
are in diuers sorts, as 
namely priuies in es&#173;
tate, priuies in deede, 
priuies in law, priuies 
in right, and priuies in 
blood. 
 
Priuies in estate is 
where a lease is made 
of the manor of dale to 
A. for life, the remain&#173;
der to B. in fee, there 
both A. and B. are pri<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
uies in estate, for their 
estates were bothe 
made at one time. And 
so is it in the first case 
heare where a lease is 
</page>
 
<page sig="160v">
made at will, for life 
or yeares or a feoffe&#173;
ment in fee, the lessees 
or feffees, are called 
priuies in estate, and 
soe are their heires 
&#38;c. 
 
Priuies in deed is 
where a lease is made 
for life, and afterward 
by an other deede the 
reuersion is graunted 
to a straunger in fee, 
thys grauntee of the 
reuersion is called 
pryuie in deede, bee&#173;
cause that he hath the 
reuersion by deede. 
 
Priuie in lawe is 
where there is Lord &#38; 
tenant, the tenant les&#173;
seth the tenauncy for 
life and dieth without 
heire, &#38; the reuersion 
escheates to the lorde, 
he is said priuy in law 
beecause that he hath 
his estate onely by the 
lawe, that is to say by 
escheate. 
 
Priuie in ryght, is 
where on possessed of a 
</page>
 
<page sig="161r">
terme for yeres, gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ts 
his estate to another 
vpon condicion, and 
maketh his executors 
&#38; dyeth, now these ex&#173;
ecutors are priuies in 
right, for if the condi&#173;
cion be broken, &#38; they 
enter into the lande, 
they shal haue it in the 
right of their testator, 
&#38; to his vse. Priuie of 
bloode is <expan type="y+e">the</expan> heire of the 
feoffor or donor &#38;c. 
 
Also if a fine bee le&#173;
uied, the heires of him 
that leuyeth the fine 
are called priuies.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="privilege(n)">&#182; Priuiledges.</form>
<xpln lang="en">PRiuiledges are ly&#173;
berties and fraun&#173;
chises graunted to an 
Office, place, towne, 
or mannour, by the 
Queenes great char&#173;
ter, letters patentes, 
or acte of Parliament, 
as Tolle, sake, socke, 
Infangtheefe, Out&#173;
fangtheefe, Turne 
</page>
 
<page sig="161v">
tolle, Oredelfe, and

ces.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="next friend(n)">&#182; Next friende.</form>
<xpln lang="en">NExt friende and 
wardeine in So&#173;
cage is all one, and is 
where a manne seysed 
of landes holden in 
Socage dyeth, hys is&#173;
sue within age of 14. 
yeares, then the next 
friende, or next of 
kynne to whom the 
lands cannot come or 
discende, shall haue 
the keepynge of the 
heire, &#38; of the land, to 
the onely vse of the 
heire, vntyll he come

&#38; th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> at that yeres he 
may enter &#38; put hym 
out. &#38; bring him to ac&#173;
compt: but in that ac&#173;
compt he shalbe allo&#173;
wed for all reasona&#173;
ble costes &#38; expences, 
</page>
 
<page sig="162r">
bestowed eyther vpon 
the heire or his land. 
 
And the next friend 
or next of kynne to 
whom the inhery&#173;
taunce cannot dys&#173;
cende, is thus to bee 
vnderstoode: If the 
landes discende to the 
heyre from hys fa&#173;
ther, or anye of the 
kynne of hys fathers 
side: then the mother, 
or other of the mo&#173;
thers side, are called 
the next of kynne to 
whom the inheritance 
cannot dyscende, for 
before that it shal so 
dyscende, it shall ra&#173;
ther Escheat to the 
Lorde of whom it is 
holden. And so it is 
to bee vnderstoode, 
where the landes 
came to the Heyre 
from hys Mother, 
or any of the kynne 
of hys mothers syde: 
Then the father or o&#173;
ther of the fathers 
side, are called the next 
</page>
 
<page sig="162v">
of kynne to whom the 
inheritaunce cannot 
discende: but shal ra&#173;
ther escheat to the 
Lorde of whome it is 
holden.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="protestation(n)">&#182; Protestation.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sequel(n)">PRotestation is a sa&#173;
uinge to the partie 
(that so pleadeth by 
protestation) to bee 
concluded by any mat&#173;
ter alledged or obiec&#173;
ted against him, vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
which he cannot ioin 
issu: And is no other 
thing but an exclusion 
of the conclusion, for 
hee that taketh the 
protestation excludes 
the other party to c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>&#173;
clude hym. And this 
protestatyon ought to 
stande wyth the se&#173;
quele of the plee, &#38; not 
to be repugnaunt, or 
otherwise contrary.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="purchase(n)">&#182; Purchase.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="163r">
<xpln lang="en">PUrchase is the pos&#173;
session that a man

ments by his owne act 
meanes or <emend err="ageement">agreement</emend>, 
and not by title of dis&#173;
cent, from any of hys

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="quarantine(n)">&#182; Quarentine.</form>
<xpln lang="en">QUarentine, ys 
where a man dy&#173;
eth seysed of a man&#173;
nour, place, and other 
landes whereof hys 
wife ought to bee en&#173;
dowed, then the wo&#173;
man shal hold the ma&#173;
nour place xl. dayes, 
within whiche tyme 
her dower shalbee as&#173;
signed. But if shee 
marrie within the xl. 
dayes, she shall loose 
her quarentine.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="fifteen(n)">&#182; Fifteene.</form>
<xpln lang="en">FIfteene, is a pay&#173;
ment graunted in 
Parliament to the 
</page>
 
<page sig="163v">
Queene, by the tem&#173;
poraltie, namely the 
15. part of their goods: 
And was vsed in aun&#173;
cient time to be leuied 
vppon their cattel go&#173;
yng in their grounds, 
which thynge was 
very troublesome, and 
therefore nowe for the 
most part, that way 
is alltered, and they 
vse to leuy the same 
by the yarde, or Acre 
or other measu<expan type="r'">re</expan> of l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d 
By meanes where of 
it is now lesse trouble&#173;
some, and more certen, 
then before it was. 
And euery towne and 
countrey doe knowe, 
what summe is to bee 
paied amonge them, &#38; 
how the same shalbee 
raised. We read that 
Moyses was the first 
that did number <expan type="y+e">the</expan> peo&#173;
ple, for he numbred the 
Israelites, &#38; therefore 
the first taxe, subsidye,

</page>
 
<page sig="164r">
the Hebrewes, as Po&#173;
lidor Virgill dothe

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="regrator(n)">&#182; Regrator.</form>
<xpln lang="en">REgrator is he that

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="rejoinder(n)">&#182; Reioynder.</form>

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="relief(n)">&#182; Relyfe.</form>
<xpln lang="en">RElife is sometims 
a certein some of 
money that the heire 
shal pay to the lord of 
whom those lands are 
holden, which after 
the decease of his aun&#173;
cestour are to him dis&#173;
cended as next heire: 
sometimes it is the 
paiement of an other 
thinge, and not mony: 
And therefore reliefe 
is not certaine, and a&#173;
like for all tenures, 
but euery sundry te&#173;
nure hath (for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> most 
part<emend err=" (">) </emend>hys specyall 
Reliefe certaine in it 
selfe. Neyther is it to 
be paied alwaies at a 
</page>
 
<page sig="165r">
certaine age, but vari&#173;
eth there also accor&#173;
dinge to the tenure. 
As if the tenant had 
l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds hold<expan type="e+_">en</expan> by knights 
seruice (except great 
Sergeancy) and dye 
his heire being of full 
age, and helde his l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>de 
by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> seruice of a whole 
knightes fee, the lorde 
of whom that landes 
are so holden shal haue 
of the heire C.s. in 
the name of reliefe, &#38; 
if he held by lesse then 
a knightes fee, he shall 
pay lesse, &#38; if more th<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
more, hauinge respect 
alwaies to the rate 
for euery knightes fee 
an honored shillings. 
And if hee helde by 
Graunde Serieancye 
(which is alwayes 
of the Queene, and is 
also Knyghtes ser&#173;
uice) thent he reliefe 
shall bee the value of 
the lande by the yere, 
beesides all charges is&#173;
suing out of the same. 
</page>
 
<page sig="165v">
Reliefe that the lord 
shall haue for landes 
holden in Socage, is 
so much more as the 
rent that the tenaunt 
holdeth his lande in 
Socage by, as if hee 
holde by a penny rent 
and dye, the lorde shal 
haue that penny rent, 
and a penny ouer for 
relife, of what age so&#173;
euer the tenant be, at 
the death of his aun&#173;
cestour. And note that 
in some cases the lord 
shall haue his reliefe 
immediatly after the 
death of his tenant, if 
it so be, that the time 
of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> yere wil suffre the 
same to be gotten, as 
mony, corne, flesh, fish, 
spices, or any such like 
&#38; for default of paye&#173;
ment, the lorde maye 
therefore of common 
right pres<expan type="e+_">en</expan>tly distrein 
 
But in some ca&#173;
ses the lord must stay 
for hys reliefe a cer&#173;
taine time wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> neces&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="166r">
sitye so constraineth. 
As if the tenant helde 
by a rose, a cherry, a 
<emend err="stawberry">strawberry</emend>, or such like 
and dye in winter, he 
shal not haue reliefe 
til roses, cherries, and 
straweberries are na&#173;
turally fresh and ripe, 
which is about Mid&#173;
somer, and th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> he shall 
haue one for rent, and 
an other for reliefe. 
 
There is an other 
kinde of reliefe that is 
paied after the death 
change, or alienation 
of freholders that hold 
in auncient demesne, 
and otherwise, and is 
paied as a knowledge 
of the tenure betwen 
the lord and the ten<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t. 
The same is not cer&#173;
taine how much, but 
doth varye accordinge 
to the custome of the 
mannor, or tenure and 
is to be presented by 
the Homage or Su&#173;
tors at the next court 
day of the same manor 
</page>
 
<page sig="166v">
And note that al&#173;
waies when the relief 
is due, it must be paid 
at one whole payment 
and not by partes, al&#173;
though that the rent 
be to be paied at seue&#173;
ral feastes.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="remainder(n)">&#182; Remainder.</form>

.<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="receipt(n)">&#182; Resceipt.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="reservation(n)">&#182; Reseruation.</form>
<xpln lang="en">REseruation, is ta&#173;
ken diuers waies, 
and hath diuers na&#173;
tures, as sometimes 
by way of exception

a man had before in 
him, as if a lease bee

ground reseruing the

<expan type="y+e">the</expan> lessee may not medle

the lessees, for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> gro<expan type="u+_">un</expan>d

vpon not reserued &#38;c. 
 
Sometimes a reser&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="168r">

uing yerely for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> same 
xx. li. &#38;c. And dyuers 
other such reseruati&#173;

And note that in

whether flesh, fishe,

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="retraxit(n)">&#182; Retraxit.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="reeve(n)">&#182; Reeue.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="grieve(n)">REeue is an officer, 
but more knowen 
in auncient tyme then 
at this day. For al&#173;
most euerie manor had 
then a Reeue, and yet 
still in many Copye 
holde manors (where

thing preuayleth) the 
name and office is not 
altogether forgotten. 
And is in effect that 
which now euery bai&#173;
life of a mannor prac&#173;
tiseth: although the 
name of Bailife was 
not then in vre among 
vs being since brought 
</page>
 
<page sig="169r">
in by the Normans: 
But <expan type="y+e">the</expan> name of Reeue, 
auncyently called Ge&#173;
reue, (which particle 
(Ge) in continuance of 
time was altogether 
left out and lost) came 
from <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Saxon woord 
<term lang="sx">Geresa</term>, which signyfi&#173;
eth a ruler: And so in 
dede his rule &#38; auctho&#173;
ritie was large with&#173;
in the compas of hys 
Lordes mannour and 
amonge his men and 
tenauntes as well in 
matters of gouerne&#173;
ment in peace &#38; warre, 
as in the skilfull vse 
and trade of husban&#173;
dry: For as hee did ga&#173;
ther his Lords rents, 
pay Reprises, or due&#173;
tyes issuinge out of 
the mannor: set the 
seruauntes to worke, 
fell and cutt downe 
Trees to repaire the 
buildinges, and en&#173;
closures, with dy&#173;
uers such like for his 
Lordes commoditye: 
</page>
 
<page sig="169v">
So also hee had auc&#173;
thoritie to gouerne &#38; 
keepe the tenaunts in 
peace, &#38; if neede requi&#173;
red, to leade the forth 
in warre.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="reversion(n)">&#182; Reuersion.</form>
<xpln lang="en">REuersion of lande. 
is a certeine estate 
remaininge in the les&#173;
sor or donor, after the 
particuler estate &#38; pos&#173;
session conueyed to an 
other. 
 
And it is called a re&#173;
uersion in respecte of 
the possession sepera&#173;
ted from it: so that hee 
that hath the one hath 
not the other at the 
same time, for being in 
one bodye together, 
there cannot be said a 
reuersion, because by <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
vniting, the one of th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>
is drowned in the o&#173;
ther: And so the re&#173;
uersion of land, is the 
land it selfe when it 
saueth.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="sokeman(n)">&#182; Sokmans.</form>

</page>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="spoliation(n)">&#182; Spoliation</form>
<xpln lang="en">SPoliation is a suit 
for the fruites of a 
church or for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> church 
it selfe, and it is to bee 
sued in the spirytuall 
Court, and not in our 
courts. And this suit 
lieth for one inc<expan type="u+_">um</expan>bent 
against an other in&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="173v">
<emend err="cumbnt">cumbent</emend>, where they 
both claime by one pa&#173;
tron, and where the 
right of the patronage 
doth not not come in 
question or debate. As 
if a person be created 
a bishoppe, and hath 
dispensation to keepe 
his benefice still, and 
afterward the patron 
presents an other in&#173;
cumbent which is in&#173;
stituted, and inducted: 
Nowe the Bishoppe 
may haue against that 
incumbent a Spolia&#173;
tion in the spirituall 
Court, beecause they 
claime both by one pa&#173;
tron, and the right of 
the patronage doth 
not come in debate, &#38; 
because that the other 
incumbent came to the 
possession of the bene&#173;
fice by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> course of the 
spirituall law, that is 
to say by instituti<expan type="o+_">on</expan> &#38; 
induction, so that hee 
hath colour to haue it 
&#38; be person by the es&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="174r">
pritual law, for other 
wise if he be not insti&#173;
tuted and inducted &#38;c. 
Spoliation lieth not 
against him, but ra&#173;
ther a writt of Tres&#173;
pas, or an assise of no&#173;
uel disseisin &#38;c. 
 
So it is also where 
a personne doth accept 
an other benefice, by 
reason whereof the 
patrone presentes an 
other clerke who is 
instituted &#38; inducted, 
now the one of them 
may haue Spoliation 
against the other, and 
then shal come in de&#173;
bate if he haue plura&#173;
lity or not. And so it 
is of depriuation &#38;c. 
 
The same lawe, is 
where one saieth to <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
patron, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> his clerke is 
dead, where vppon he 
presentes an other: 
There the first in&#173;
cumbent which was 
supposed to bee deade 
may haue a spoliati<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
against the other, &#38; so 
</page>
 
<page sig="174v">
in dyuers other such 
like cases.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="testament(n)">&#182; Testament.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="nuncupative(a)"  lexeme="testament(n)">TEstament is thus 
defined or expoun&#173;
ded in master Plow&#173;
dens comentaries, a 
testament is the wit&#173;
nes of the minde, and 
is compound of these 
</page>
 
<page sig="176v">
two wordes. <term lang="la">Testa&#173;
tio &#38; mentis</term>, which so 
signifieth, trueth is, 
that a Testament is 
a witnes of the minde. 
but that it is a com&#173;
pounde worde, Aulus 
Gellius in his vj. booke 
cap. 12. doth deny the 
same to an excellent 
Lawyer one Seruius 
Sulpicius, and sayeth 
that it is a simple 
worde, as are these: 
<term lang="la">Calciamentum, Paluda&#173;
mentum paumentum</term>, 
and dyuers such like: 
And much lesse is <term lang="la">a&#173;
greamentum</term> a com&#173;
pounde worde of <term lang="la">ag&#173;
gregatio</term>, and <term lang="la">mentium</term>
as is sayde beefore in 
that tytle, for there 
is noe suche latyne 
worde simple or com&#173;
pounde, but it may 
neuer the lesse serue 
well for a lawe latyn 
worde. 
 
And therefore thus 
it may bee better de&#173;
fined. A Testament 
</page>
 
<page sig="177r">
is the true declara&#173;
tion of our last wyll, 
of that we would to 
be don after out death 
&#38;c. And of Testam<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts 
there be ij. sorts, name 
lye a Testament in 
writing, &#38; a Testa&#173;
m<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t by woords which 
is called a Nuncupa&#173;
tiue testament. 
 
The first is alwayes 
in writing as is sayd. 
 
The other is when 
a man beeing sicke, and 
for feare least death or 
want of memorie, or 
of speach, should come 
so suddenly and haste&#173;
ly vpon him that hee 
should be preuented if 
he stayed the writing 
of his testament, de&#173;
sireth his neyghbours 
and friendes to beare 
witnesse of his laste 
will, and then decla&#173;
reth the same present&#173;
ly by wordes before 
them, which after his 
decease is prooued by 
wytnesses, and put 
</page>
 
<page sig="177v">
in writing by the Or&#173;
dinarie, &#38; then stan&#173;
eth in as good force, 
(except for lands) as 
if it had at the first in 
the life of the testator 
ben put in writing.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="toll(n)" lexeme="tolne(n)">&#182; Tolle, or Tolne.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="turn(v)" lexeme="traverse(a)" lexeme="through(a)">TOlle or Tolne, is 
most properlye a 
payment vsed in Ci&#173;
ties, townes, markets 
&#38; faires for goods and 
</page>
 
<page sig="179r">
cattel brought thither 
to bee bought &#38; solde. 
And is alwaies to bee 
paied by the buyer, &#38; 
not by the seller, ex&#173;
cept there be some cus&#173;
tome otherwise. 
 
There are diuers o&#173;
ther tolles, as Turne 
tolle, &#38; that is where 
toll is paied for beasts 
that are dryuen to bee 
solde, although that 
they bee not solde in 
deede. 
 
Also Tolle trauers,

meth to haue a halfe&#173;
peny, or such like toll 
of euery beast that is 
driuen ouer his gro<expan type="u+_">un</expan>d. 
 
Through tolle, is 
where a Towne pre&#173;
scribes to haue tol for 
euery beast that goeth 
through their towne 
a certein: or for euery 
score or 100. a certein, 
which seemeth not to 
bee so vnreasonable a 
prescription or cust<expan type="o+_">om</expan>e 
as some haue thought 
</page>
 
<page sig="179v">
although it be through 
the Queenes hyghe

where euery man may

there be one thing for 
another, as if there be

commoditie prouyded 
at the costes &#38; charges 
of the Towne, for the 
ease of trauaylers <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
driue that way, where 
by theyr iourney ys 
either shortned or bet&#173;
tered, why then may 
not tolle be lawfully 
and with good reason 
dema<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ded of them &#38;c. 
But diuers Citiz<expan type="e+_">en</expan>s &#38; 
Townes men are free 
from paying tolle by

or her auncestors, or 
do claime the same by

tome. So also spiry&#173;
tual persons &#38; religi&#173;
ous men (as they call

ing tol for their goods 
&#38; march<expan type="a+_">an</expan>dises bought 
</page>
 
<page sig="180r">
and sold, but now the

8. will that they shall 
not marchandise. But 
enquyre whether the

some say it is not. 
 
Also tenants in aun<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
cient demesne ought 
to be quite thorough 
the whole Realme of 
paying tolle, as appea&#173;

Sokemans. And in al 
these cases where toll 
is dema<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ded where it 
ought not to be paied 
of th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> that should go, 
buy, &#38; sell tolle free 
there <expan type="y+e">the</expan> partie or par&#173;
ties greued may haue 
a writ, <term lang="la">De effendi quie&#173;

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="view(n)">&#182; Viewe</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="viscount(n)">&#182; Viscount.</form>

latine worde <term lang="la">Portus</term>,

And thus was the

Thus much is sayde

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="voucher(n)">&#182; Voucher.</form>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="use(n)">&#182; Vses.</form>
<xpln lang="en">VSes of lande had 
beginning after <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
<emend err="the"></emend> custome of proper&#173;
tie began among men. 
As where one beeyng 
seised of landes in fee 
simple, made a feoffe&#173;

</page>
 
<page sig="184r">
H. 8 cap. 10. prouided, 
which vniteth the vse 
&#38; possession together, 
so that who hath the 
vse of lande, the same 
hath <expan type="y+e">the</expan> possession ther&#173;
of. by vertue of that 
estatute.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="usury(n)">&#182; Vsurie.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="divorce(n)">VSurie, is a gayne 
of any thing aboue 
the principal, or that 
which was lent, exac&#173;
ted onely in conside&#173;
ration of the loane, 
whether it be of corn, 
meat, apparel, wares, 
or such like, as of 
money. And here 
much myght be saied, 
and many cases might 
bee putt concernynge 
Vsurie, whiche of 
purpose I omytte, 
onely I wyshe, that 
they who accompte 
th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>selues religious &#38; 
good christians, would 
not deceiue th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>selues 
</page>
 
<page sig="184v">
by colour of the sta&#173;
tute of vsurie, because 
it sayeth that it shall 
not be lawful for any 
to take aboue x. ii. in 
the C. li. for a yere &#38;c. 
whereby they gather 
(although falsly) that 
they may therefore 
take x. li. for the loane 
of an C. li. with a good 
conscience, because the 
Statute doth after a 
sort dispence withal, 
(for that it doth not 
punish such taking,) 
which thing it cannot 
do with the lawes &#38; 
ordin<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ces of God, for 
God will haue his de&#173;
crees to be kept inuio&#173;
lable, who sayth, lende 
looking for nothynge 
thereby &#38;c. By which 
woordes is excluded, 
eyther the taking of 
x. li. v. li. yea, or one 
penny aboue the prin&#173;
cipall. But rather let 
such think, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> that sta&#173;
tute was made vppon 
like cause, that moued 
</page>
 
<page sig="185r">
Moyses to gyue a 
bill of dyuorce to the 
Isralites, as name&#173;
lye to auoyde a grea&#173;
ter mischiefe, and for 
the hardnesse of their 
hartes.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="outlawry(n)">&#182; Vtlawrie.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="exigent(n)">VTlawry is wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> an 
exigent goeth forth 
against any m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>, &#38; pro&#173;
clamation made at v. 
co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ties, then at the v. 
countye if the def. ap&#173;
pere not, the coroner 
shal giue iudgement <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
he shalbe out of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> pro&#173;
tection of the Queene, 
&#38; out of the aide of the 
lawe, and by such an 
vtlary in actions per&#173;
sonals, the party out&#173;
lawed shall forfayt al 
his goodes and cattels 
to the Queene. And by 
an vtlary in felony, hee 
shall forfait aswel all 
his landes, and tene&#173;
ments that he hath in 
fee simple, or for terme 
</page>
 
<page sig="185v">
of his life: as his 
good &#38; <emend err="catttals">cattals</emend>. And 
though a man be out&#173;
lawed, yet if any er&#173;
ror or discontinuance 
be in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> suit of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> proces 
the party thereof shal 
haue aduantage, &#38; for 
such cause the vtlary 
shalbe reuersed &#38; ad&#173;
nulled. Or if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> partye 
defendant be ouer the 
sea at <expan type="y+e">the</expan> time of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> vtla&#173;
ry prono<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ced that is 
a good cause of the re&#173;
uersal of the vtlary. 
 
If an exigent be awar<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ded against a man in 
one co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ty where hee 
dwelleth not yet an 
exig<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t <expan type="w+t">with</expan> proclamati<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
shal go forth to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
ty where he dwelleth: 
or els if he be thervp<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
vtlawed, <expan type="y+e">the</expan> vtlary may 
be reuersed as it appe&#173;
reth by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> statute made 
the 4 yere of King H. 
8. And if a man be out 
lawed in an acti<expan type="o+_">on</expan> per&#173;
sonal at <expan type="y+e">the</expan> suit of an o&#173;
ther, and after he pur&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="186r">
chase his charter of 
pardon of the Queen, 
such charter shal ne&#173;
uer be allowed, til hee 
hath sued a writte of 
<term lang="la">Scire facias</term> to warne 
the partye plaintife, 
and if he appeare, then 
the defendant shal an&#173;
swere him, and barre 
him of his action, or 
els make agreement 
with him.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="waif(n)">&#182; Waife.</form>
<xpln lang="en">WAyfe is when a 
theefe hath felo&#173;
niously stolne goodes, 
and beinge neerelye 
followed with hue, 
and crye, or els ouer&#173;
charged with the bur&#173;
den or trouble of the 
goodes, for his ease 
sake and more speedye 
trauailinge, without 
hue and cry, flieth a&#173;
way and leaueth the 
goods or any part of 
them behind him, then 
the queenes officer or 
</page>
 
<page sig="186v">
the Reeue, or Bailife 
to the Lord of the ma&#173;
nour (within whose 
Iurisdiction or circuit 
they were left) that 
by prescriptyon, or 
gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>t fr<expan type="o+_">om</expan> the Queene 
hath the fraunchise of 
waife, may seyse the 
goodes so wayued to 
their lordes vse, who 
may keepe them as his 
owne proper goods: 
except that the owner 
come with fresh suite 
after the felon, &#38; sue 
an appeale, or giue in 
euidence against him 
at his arrainem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
the indictment, and be 
attainted thereof &#38;c. 
In which cases <expan type="y+e">the</expan> first 
owner shall haue res&#173;
titution of his goodes 
so stollen and way&#173;
ued. 
 
But although as 
hath byn sayd wayfe 
is properly of goodes 
stollen, yet wayfe 
may bee also the goods 
that are not stolne. 
</page>
 
<page sig="187r">
As if a man bee pur&#173;
sued wyth hue, and 
crye, as a felon, and 
hee flyeth, and leaueth 
his owne goodes &#38;c. 
these shalbe taken as 
good wayued, &#38; for&#173;
fait as if they had bin 
stolne.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="waive(n)">&#182; Waiue.</form>
<xpln lang="en">WAiue is a wom<expan type="a+_">an</expan>
that is autlawed, 
&#38; she is called waiue, 
as left out or forsaken 
of the law, and not an 
vtlawe as a man is. 
For women are not 
sworne in leetes to the 
lawe, as menn are, 
whoe therefore are 
within <expan type="y+e">the</expan> law, where&#173;
as women are not, 
and for that cause 
they cannot bee sayd 
out of the lawe in so 
much as they neuer 
were within it. But a 
man is called vtlawe, 
beecause that hee was 
</page>
 
<page sig="187v">
once sworne to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> law: 
&#38; now for contempt he 
is put out of the law, 
&#38; is called vtlawe, as 
one shoulde say <expan type="w+t">with</expan>out 
benefite of the law.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="wardwite(n)">&#182; Warwite.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="watch(n)">WArwite (or ward 
wite as some co&#173;
pies haue it) that is 
to bee quite of giuing 
of money for keeping 
of watches.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="wreck(n)">&#182; Wrecke.</form>
<xpln lang="en">WRecke or <term lang="fr">varech</term>
as the Normans 
from whom it came 
call it, is where a ship 
is perished on the sea, 
and no man escapeth 
a liue out of the same, 
and the shippe, or part 
of the ship so perished, 
or the goods of the ship 
come to the lande of a&#173;
ny Lorde, the Lorde 
shall haue that as a 
wreck of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> sea, but if a 
</page>
 
<page sig="188r">
man, or a dogg, or cat, 
escape a liue, so that <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
partye to whome the 
goods belong come <expan type="w+t">with</expan>&#173;
in a yere and a day and 
proue the goods to bee 
his, he shal haue th<expan type="e+_">em</expan> a 
gaine, by prouision of 
the statute of West. <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
I. cap. 4. made in king 
Ed. I. daies, who there 
in followed the decree 
of Henry the first, be&#173;
fore whose daies, if a 
shippe had ben cast on 
shore, torne with tem&#173;
pest, and were not re&#173;
paired by such as es&#173;
caped a lyue within a 
certeyne tyme, that 
then this was taken 
for wrecke.</xpln></wordentry>

<wordentry type="h"><form lang="fr">&#182; Seruice de chiualer.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="escuage(n)">TO holde by 
knightes ser&#173;
uice, is to holde 
by homage, fe&#173;
alty, &#38; escuage, 
and it draweth to it 
warde, mariage, &#38; re&#173;
liefe, and knowe thou 
that knightes seruice 
is seruice of landes or 
tenementes to beare 
armes in warre in the 
defence of the Realme, 
&#38; it oweth warde in the 
defence of the Realme, 
&#38; it oweth warde and 
mariage by reas<expan type="o+_">on</expan> that 
none is able nor of 
power, nor may haue 
knowledge to beare 
armes, before <expan type="y+t">that</expan> he be of 
the age of 21. yeres. 
And for so much <expan type="y+t">that</expan> the 
lord shal not leese that 
that of right he ought 
to haue, &#38; that <expan type="y+e">the</expan> power 
of the realme, nothing 
be made weake. The 
law wil because of his 
tender age, that the 
Lord him shal haue in 
his warde till the full 
</page>
 
<page sig="189r">
age of him, that is to 
say xxj. yeres.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="grand serjeanty(n)">&#182; Graunde serieantie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold by graund 
serieanty is as if a 
man hold certein l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
or tenementes of the 
king to go with him 
in his host, or to beare 
his banner with him 
in his warres, or to 
leade his host, or such 
like, and thereto bee&#173;
longeth warde mary&#173;
age and relyefe, as it 
appeareth in the trea&#173;
tise of wards and re&#173;
liefes in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> statute made 
the 28. of Edwarde 
the I.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="petit serjeanty(n)">&#182; Petit Serieantie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO holde by petit 
serieantie is as if a 
man hold of the kinge 
landes or tenementes, 
yelding to him a knife, 
a buckler, an Arrowe, 
a Bow <expan type="w+t">with</expan>out stringe, 
</page>
 
<page sig="189v">
or other like seruice at 
the will of the first 
feoffour, and there be&#173;
longeth not warde 
maryage ne relyefe. 
And marke well that 
a man may not holde 
by graunde nor petit 
serieantie, but of the 
King.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="escuage(n)">&#182; Escuage.</form>
<xpln lang="en">To hold by escuage is 
by knightes seruice, &#38; 
there belongeth ward, 
mariage, and reliefe. 
And marke well that 
a man may not holde 
by escuage, but that 
hee holde by homage, 
for that escuage of 
common ryght dra&#173;
weth to him homage, 
as it was Iudged 
<term lang="la">Termino</term> H. 21. E. 
3. cap. 42. fol. 52. 
Auowrye 115. And 
note well, that es&#173;
cuage is a certeyne 
summe of money, and 
</page>
 
<page sig="190r">
it ought to bee leuyed 
by the Lord of his te&#173;
nant after the quanti&#173;
tie of his tenure, when 
escuage runneth by al 
Englande. And it is 
ordeined by al the co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
sell of England how 
much euery tenaunt 
shal geue to his Lord, 
and that is properlye 
for to maintayne the 
warres betwene Eng&#173;
land, &#38; them of Scot&#173;
lande or of Wales, 
and not beetwene o&#173;
ther landes, for that, 
<expan type="y+t">that</expan> those foresayd lands 
should be of ryght be&#173;
longinge to the Re&#173;
alme of England.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="homage(n)" lexeme="ancestral(a)">&#182; Homage auncestrel.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO holde by homage 
auncestrel is where 
I or my auncestours 
haue hold<expan type="e+_">en</expan> of you &#38; of 
your auncestors from 
time out of mind wher 
of no minde runneth, 
</page>
 
<page sig="190v">
by homage, fealty, and 
certaine rent. And it 
is not to holde by 
knightes seruice, and 
there belongeth not 
ward, mariage, nor 
reliefe. And note well 
that homage may bee 
said in ij. maners, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is 
to say, homage ances&#173;
trel, &#38; <term lang="fr">homage de fait</term>
Homage auncestrel is 
where you or your an&#173;
cestors haue holden of 
me and mine aunces&#173;
tors during the time 
of mans rem<expan type="e+_">em</expan>brance, 
by homage, fealty, and 
r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t. <term lang="fr">Homage de fait</term> is 
where I enfeffe your 
selfe, to hold of mee by 
homage and rent, and 
in so much that this 
homage beginneth by 
my deede, it is called 
homage de fait. 
 
And note wel that 
Homage auncestrell 
draweth to him vou&#173;
cher, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> is to say, war&#173;
r<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ty of auncestors, but 
not <term lang="fr">homage de fait</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="191r">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="courtesy(n)" lexeme="England(pn)">&#182; Curtesy of England.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold by the cur&#173;
tesy of Englande 
is there where a man 
taketh a wife inheri&#173;
trix, &#38; they haue issue 
a sonne or daughter, &#38; 
the wife dieth, whe&#173;
ther the issue be deade 
or aliue, <expan type="y+e">the</expan> husb<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d shal 
hold this l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d for term 
of his life by the cur&#173;
tesy of England, &#38; by 
the law. And in this 
case the fee &#38; the right 
remaineth in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> person 
of him of whom he hol<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
deth: and for that, this 
tenant may not alyen 
in fee, nor for terme of 
anothers life, &#38; if he do 
it is lawful to him in <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
reuersion to enter.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="fee simple(n)">&#182; Fee simple.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in fee sim&#173;
ple is to hold to a&#173;
ny man or woman, to 
him &#38; to his heirs and 
his assignes for euer.</xpln></wordentry>
</page>
 
<page sig="191v">
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="frank tenure(n)">&#182; Franke tenure.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in free hold 
is to hold for terme 
of his owne lyfe, or 
for terme of an other 
mans life. And in this 
case the fee &#38; the right 
remaineth in the per&#173;
son of him, of whome 
he holdeth. And for <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
this tenaunt may not 
alien in fee nor for 
terme of life: And if he 
do, it is well lawfull 
to him in whom the 
fee &#38; the right abideth 
to enter.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="dower(n)">&#182; Dower.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in dower is 
where a man inhe&#173;
rite taketh a wife and 
dieth, the heire shal en&#173;
ter, &#38; endow the wyfe 
of the third part of al 
that <expan type="y+t">that</expan> was to her hus&#173;
band in his life, in fee 
simple or fee taile, and 
shee shall holde these 
landes for terme of 
</page>
 
<page sig="192r">
her lyfe as her free 
holde.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="fr">&#182; Terme dans.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="termor(n)" lexeme="chattel(n)">TO hold for terme of 
yeares is not but 
chattel in effect, for no 
action is maintenable 
against the termour, 
for the recouering of 
the freehold for no free 
hold is in him. A leas 
for terme of yeares is 
a chattel reall, and 
the other chattel per&#173;
sonall, and all goods 
whych are remoua&#173;
ble are chattelles per&#173;
sonals.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="mortgage(n)">&#182; Mortgage.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="donee(n)">TO hold in morgage 
is to hold for a cer&#173;
taine terme vpon con&#173;
dition, that if the les&#173;
sor pay so much mony 
at such a day, that hee 
may enter, and if not, 
that <expan type="y+e">the</expan> other shal haue 
a fee simple or fee taile, 
or free holde. And in 
</page>
 
<page sig="192v">
euery case where l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
or tenements be geuen 
to a man for a certeine 
terme vpon condition 
of the part of the lessor 
for to make the lessee 
to haue more l<expan type="o+_">on</expan>g time 
or terme, if the other do 
not as the condition 
is, the landes and te&#173;
nementes vntyll the 
daye that the con&#173;
dicyon shoulde bee 
done, bee holden in 
morgage, as in a dead 
gage. 
 
And note well that 
if land be let to a man 
in morgage in fee sim&#173;
ple or in fee taile vpon 
condition, that if the 
first lessor, as is before 
said, pay so much mo&#173;
ney at such a day that 
he may enter, &#38; if not, 
that the lessee haue the 
same estate in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> lands, 
that the lessour dyd 
him graunt at the be&#173;
ginninge. And if be&#173;
fore the day assigned, 
the lessee bee disseised, 
</page>
 
<page sig="193r">
he shall haue assise of 
nouel disseisin. And in 
case that if the lessee 
take a wife &#38; dye sey&#173;
sed before the day as&#173;
signed, the wom<expan type="a+_">an</expan> shall 
be endowed. 
 
And note well, that 
if the lessor after the 
death of the lessee pay 
not the money, at the 
day assigned, then the 
woman shall hold her 
dower, and the issue 
his heritage. And in 
case the lessour at the 
day assigned pay the 
money to the heire o f 
the lessee, then he may 
put out the woman &#38; 
the heire also of al the 
land first let. And if a 
man geeue lands to an 
other in the taile, yel&#173;
ding to him a certeine 
rent by the yere, &#38; one 
enter for default of 
payment, the donee ta&#173;
keth a wife and dyeth 
seised, the woman shal 
be endowed. And in 
case that after the rent 
</page>
 
<page sig="193v">
be behind, the donour 
may enter &#38; put out 
the woman &#38; the heire 
also. And note well, 
that if landes be let to 
a man in Morgage in 
fee vpon condicion, the 
lessee doth alien, the 
lessour shal bee char&#173;
ged to pay the mo&#173;
ney to the alienee, and 
not to the feoffee, as 
it is saide.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="burgage(n)">&#182; Burgage.</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="194r">
<xpln lang="en">TO holde in Bur&#173;
gage, is to holde as 
if the Burgeis holde 
of the king, or of ano&#173;
ther Lord lands or te&#173;
nements, yelding to 
him a certeine rent by 
the yeare, or els there 
where another man 
then burge is holdeth 
of any Lord landes or 
tenem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts in burgage, 
yelding to him a cer&#173;
tein rent by yeare.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="socage(n)">&#182; Socage.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in Socage 
is to holde of any 
Lord landes or tene&#173;
ments, yelding to him 
a certeine rent by the 
yere for al maner ser&#173;
uices. And note wel, 
that to holde by So&#173;
cage is not to holde by 
knightes seruice, nor 
there belongeth ward, 
mariage, nor relyefe, 
but they shall double 
once their rent after <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
death of their aunces&#173;
tors according to that 
that they be wont to 
pay to their lord. And 
they shall not be ouer 
measure greued, as it 
appeareth in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> treatise 
of wardes &#38; reliefes. 
And note wel, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> So&#173;
cage may be said in iij. 
maners, that is to say, 
socage in free tenure, 
Socage in auncient 
tenure, and Socage in 
base tenure. Socage 
in free tenu<expan type="r'">re</expan> is to hold 
frely by certein r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t for 
all maner of seruices, 
</page>
 
<page sig="194v">
as is before said, and 
of that the next kyns 
bodie shall haue the 
warde to whom the 
heritage may not dis&#173;
cend, til the age of xiiij 
yeares, that is to say, 
if the heritage come 
by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> part of the father 
they of the part of the 
mother shall haue the 
ward, &#38; contrarywise 
 
And note wel that if 
the gardein in So&#173;
cage do make wast, he 
shall not be impeched 
of wast, but he shall 
yelde accompt to the 
heire when he shal c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>e 
to his full age of xxj. 
yeares. And looke the 
statute of Marlebridge 
ca. 17. for this matter. 
Socage in aunci<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t te&#173;
nure is <expan type="y+t">that</expan> where the 
people in aunci<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t de&#173;
mesne helde, whych 
vse no other wryt to 
haue then the writ of 
right close, which shal 
be determined accor&#173;
ding to the custome of 
</page>
 
<page sig="195r">
the manor, &#38; the <term lang="la">Mon&#173;
strauerunt</term> for to dys&#173;
charge them wh<expan type="e+_">en</expan> their 
Lord distrayneth th<expan type="e+_">em</expan>
for to do other seruice 
<expan type="y+t">that</expan> they ought not to do 
And this writ of <term lang="la">M<expan type="o+_">on</expan>&#173;
strauerunt</term> ought to bee 
brought agaynst the 
Lord, &#38; those tenants 
hold al by one certain 
seruice, &#38; these be free 
tenaunts of auncient 
demesne. 
 
Socage in base te&#173;
nure is where a man 
holdeth in auncyent 
demesne, that may not 
haue the <term lang="la">Monstrauer<expan type="u+_">un</expan>t</term>, 
and for that it is cal&#173;
led the base Tenure.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="fee-farm(n)">&#182; Fee ferme.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in fee ferme 
is to hold in fee sim<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
ple, yelding to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> Lord 
the value, or at <expan type="y+e">the</expan> least 
the fourth part by the 
yeare, &#38; he ought to do 
no other thing, but as 
it is conteined in the 
feffement, and he that 
</page>
 
<page sig="195v">
holdeth in fee ferme 
ought to do fealtie &#38; 
not reliefe.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="frank-fee(n)">&#182; Franke fee.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO holde in franke 
fee, is to hold in fee 
simple lands pledable 
at the common law.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="base(a)" lexeme="fee(n)">&#182; Base fee.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in fee base, 
is to holde at the 
will of the Lord.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="villeinage(n)">&#182; Villenage.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="sokeman(n)">TO hold in pure vil&#173;
lenage, is to doe all 
that, that the Lorde 
wil him c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>maund. 
 
The diffinition of 
villenage is villein of 
bloud, and of tenure. 
And it is he of whom 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> Lord taketh red<expan type="e+_">em</expan>p&#173;
tion to marie his dau&#173;
ghter, &#38; to make hym 
free, &#38; it is he whom <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
Lord may put out of 
</page>
 
<page sig="196r">
his landes or tene&#173;
mentes at his will, &#38; 
also of all his goods &#38; 
cattel. And note wel, 
that a sokeman is no 
pure villein, nor a vil&#173;
lein oweth not ward, 
mariage, nor reliefe, 
nor to do any other 
seruices reall. And 
note well, that the te&#173;
nure in villenage shal 
make no free man vil&#173;
lein, if it be not conti&#173;
nued sith time out of 
mind, nor villein land 
shal make no free man 
villein, nor free lande 
shal make no villeine 
free, except <expan type="y+t">that</expan> the ten<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t 
haue c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>tinued free sith 
the time of no minde, 
but a villein shal make 
free l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d villein by sei&#173;
sin or claime of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> lord. 
And note wel, that if 
a villein purchase cer&#173;
teine lande, and take a 
wife &#38; alyen, and dy&#173;
eth before the clayme 
or seisin of the lord, <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
wife shalbe endowed, 
</page>
 
<page sig="196v">
And note wel, that in 
case that <expan type="y+e">the</expan> lord bringe 
a <term lang="la">Precipe quod reddat</term> a&#173;
gainst the alien which 
voucheth to warrant 
the issue of the villein 
which is villein to <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
lord, he shal haue the 
voucher, &#38; by protes&#173;
tation the lorde may 
say <expan type="y+t">that</expan> (notwithst<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ding 
that he pled with his 
villein) yet his villein 
shal not be enfranchi&#173;
sed. And note wel <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
a bastard shall neuer 
be iudged villeine, but 
by knowledg in court 
of recorde. And note 
well that if det be due 
by a Lorde to a free 
man, and hee maketh 
two men his execu&#173;
tours the which bee 
villeines to the saide 
Lorde and dyeth, the 
villeines shal haue an 
actyon of det against 
their Lorde not with<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
standinge that hee 
plead with them. And 
if he make protestati<expan type="o+_">on</expan>
</page>
 
<page sig="197r">
they shal not be for so 
much enfranchised, for 
that that they be to 
recouer the dett afore 
said to the vse of an o&#173;
ther person that is to 
say to the vse of their 
testatour, and not to 
their owne vse. And 
if the tenant in dower 
haue a villeine which 
purchaseth certaine 
lande in fee, and after 
the tenaunt in dower 
entreth, she shal haue 
the land to her an to 
her heires for euer&#173;
more, &#38; the same lawe 
is of tenant for terme 
of yeares of a villein. 
 
And note wel that 
the lord may robb his 
villein, bete &#38; chastice 
at his wil, saue onely 
that he may not maim 
him for then he shall 
haue appel of maime a<emend err="">&#173;</emend>
gainst him. 
 
And note wel, that 
a villein may haue iij. 
acti<expan type="o+_">on</expan>s against his lord 
that is to say, appeale 
</page>
 
<page sig="197v">
of deth of his ancestor, 
appel of rape done to 
his wife, and appel of 
maime. And note wel 
if ij. parceners bringe 
a writ of niefe, and one 
of them be nonsuit, the 
nonsuit of him shal be 
iudged the nonsuit of 
them both, so that if <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
nonsuit be after appea&#173;
rance, they shal be put 
out from that actyon 
for euer, for the lawe 
is such in fauour of 
lybertye. And note 
wel, if two haue a vil&#173;
leine in common, and 
one of them make to 
him a manumission, he 
shal not be made free 
against both, And note 
well, that in a writ <term lang="la">de 
Natiuo habendo</term>, it bee&#173;
houeth that the lorde 
shew how he c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>meth 
priuy of the bloode of 
the villeine of whom 
he is lord &#38;c. And if he 
nor none of his aun&#173;
cestours were not 
seised of none of his 
</page>
 
<page sig="198r">
blood, he shal not winn 
by his action, if the 
villeine haue not kno&#173;
wledged in court of 
record him selfe to bee 
his villein. And note 
wel that in a writt of 
Niefe may not be put 
more Niefes th<expan type="e+_">en</expan> two 
and this was first 
brought in in the ha&#173;
tred of bondage. But 
in a writt <term lang="la">de libertate 
probanda</term>, may be put 
as many niefes as the 
plaintife wil. 
 
And note wel that 
if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> villein of a lord be 
in auncien demesne of 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> king, or other town 
priuiledged, within a 
yeare &#38; a day, the lord 
may seise him, &#38; if hee 
dwel in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> same towne 
or other place fr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>chi&#173;
sed by a yere &#38; a daye 
without seisin of the 
lord, he hath no pow&#173;
er to seise him after, if 
he go not in estrey out 
of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> aforesaid fra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>chis.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="tail(n)">&#182; Taile. 
</form>
</page>
 
<page sig="198v">
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in the taile 
is where a manne 
holdeth certain lands 
or tenements to hym 
&#38; to his heires of hys 
bodie begotten. And 
note wel, that if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>d 
be geeuen to a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> &#38; to 
his heires male, he hath 
fee simple, &#38; that were 
adiudged in the Par&#173;
liam<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t of our lord the 
king. But where l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
or tenem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts be geeuen 
to a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> &#38; to his heires 
males of his bodie be&#173;
gotten, then hee hath 
fee taile, &#38; the issue fe&#173;
male shal not be enhe&#173;
ritable, as it appea&#173;
reth the xiiij. yeare of 
Ed. the iij. in assise.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="tail after possibility(n)">&#182; Taile after possibilitie.</form>
<xpln lang="en">TO hold in the taile 
after possibilitie of 
issue extinct, is where 
land is geeuen to a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>
&#38; to his wife, &#38; to the 
heirz of their ij bodies 
</page>
 
<page sig="199r">
ingendred, and one of 
them ouerlyueth the 
other wythout issue 
betwene them begot&#173;
ten, he shall holde the 
land for terme of hys 
owne life, as tenant in 
the taile after possibi&#173;
litie of issue extinct. 
And notwithstanding 
that hee do wast, hee 
shal neuer bee impea&#173;
ched of that waste. 
And note that if he a&#173;
lien, he in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> reuersion 
shall not haue a writ 
of entrie <term lang="la">in <emend err="consim ili">consimili</emend>
casu</term>. But he may en&#173;
ter, &#38; his entre is law&#173;
full, <term lang="la">per</term> Rob. Thorpe 
chiefe Iustice.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="free(a)" lexeme="marriage(n)">&#182; Free Mariage.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="frank-marriage(n)">TO holde in frank&#173;
mariage, is to hold 
in the second taile ly&#173;
mitted in the statute 
of Westminst. ij. cap. I 
And the feoffor shall 
acquite the feoffee of 
all maner of seruices 
</page>
 
<page sig="199v">
vntil the 4. degree bee 
past, &#38; the feffor shal do 
al the seruice &#38; suites 
during the said terme. 
And after the heires 
of the feoffee shal do it, 
for that that the pri&#173;
uitie of bloud is past. 
And if he be distrained 
for seruice, he shal haue 
a writt of Mesne a&#173;
gainst him supposinge 
that hee held the lands 
of him, but hee shall 
not haue the fore&#173;
iudgement if it bee not 
in aduauntage of his 
issues. 
 
And note wel, that 
after the fowerth de&#173;
gree bee past, he shalbe 
attendant of as much 
seruice to the donour, 
as the donor is atten&#173;
dant to the Lorde pa&#173;
<emend err="amount">ramount</emend>. And if hee do 
felony for which hee 
is attaint, the kinge 
shal haue his lands for 
terme of his lyfe na&#173;
turall. And after hys 
death, his issue shal in&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="200r">
herite, as by force of 
the taile. And in this 
case, none shall haue 
his landes by way of 
escheate, no more then 
in any other taile. And 
in case that the tenant 
die without heire of 
his body begotten, the 
lande shall reuert to 
the donor as it should 
in the common tayle. 
And if a man let hys 
lande to another in 
<emend err="in"></emend> franke mariage yel&#173;
dinge to him a cer&#173;
tayne rent by yeare, 
hee shal hold this land 
in the common tayle, 
and not in frankenma&#173;
riage for by the rent 
reserued, these words 
(<term lang="la">in liberum maritagium</term>) 
bee al vtterly voyd, so 
that the tenure shalbe 
intended after the te&#173;
nure in the common 
taile. 
 
And note well that 
the gift in franke ma&#173;
riage hath a condicion 
annexed to it, not<expan type="w+t">with</expan>&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="200v">
standing that it be not 
openly declared in the 
deede of the gift, as it 
appeareth by the sta&#173;
tute of Westminst. ij. 
cap. I. <term lang="la">De donis condi&#173;
cionalibus</term>. 
 
And note well that 
a man shall not geeue 
lands nor tenementes 
in frankmariage, but 
where the woman is 
priuie of bloud to the 
donor, for els the man 
nor the woman shall 
haue no other estate 
by the feoffement but 
for terme of lyfe.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="free(a)" lexeme="alms(n)">&#182; Free almes.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="frankalmoign(n)">TO holde in franke 
almoigne is to hold 
landes or tenementes 
for to serue God and 
holy church to endow 
without doing any o&#173;
ther maner of seruice. 
And note wel, that in 
this case the donor is 
mesne, &#38; ought to ac&#173;
quit him freely against 
</page>
 
<page sig="201r">
the chiefe Lorde, &#38; also 
they that hold in fr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>k 
almoigne shal doe no 
fealtie, but they that 
holde in franke ma&#173;
riage, shal do fealtie.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="elegit(n)">&#182; Elegit.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="alienor(n)" lexeme="alienee(n)" lexeme="fieri-facias(n)">TO holde by Elegit 
is where a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> hath 
recouered debt or d<expan type="a+_">am</expan>&#173;
mage by a writte a&#173;
gainst another or by 
confession or in other 
maner, he shall haue 
within the yeare a&#173;
gainst him a writ Iu&#173;
diciall called Elegyt 
to haue execution of 
the halfe of al his l<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ds 
and cattelles, (except 
Oxen and beastes of 
the plowe) tyll the 
debt or dammages bee 
vtterly leuied or paied 
to him, &#38; during the 
terme he is tenaunt by 
Elegit. And note wel 
if he be put out with&#173;
in the terme hee shall 
haue assise of nouell 
</page>
 
<page sig="201v">
disseisin, and after a re&#173;
disseisin if neede be, and 
this is geuen by <expan type="y+e">the</expan> sta&#173;
tute of Westminster: 
cap. 18. &#38; also by the 
equity of the same sta&#173;
tute, he that hath his 
estate if hee be put out 
shal haue assise and a 
redisseisin if neede bee, 
and also if hee make 
his executors and die, 
and his executors en&#173;
ter and after bee put 
out, they shall haue by 
the equity of the same 
statute such action as 
hee him selfe before&#173;
sayde, but if hee bee 
put out, and after 
make his executours 
and dye, his executors 
may enter, and if they 
bee stopped of their 
entre, they shall haue 
a writte of trespasse 
vppon their matter 
and case. 
 
And note wel if hee 
do wast in al the lande 
or parcel, the other shal 
haue against him im&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="202r">
mediately a writ Iu&#173;
diciall out of the first 
recorde called a <term lang="la">veni&#173;
re facias ad computan&#173;
dum</term>, by which it shal 
bee inquired if he haue 
leuyed all the money, 
or parcell, and if hee 
haue not leuyed the 
money, then it shalbee 
inquired to how much 
the wast amounteth, 
and if the waste a&#173;
mount but to parcel, 
then as much of the 
money, as the wast 
amounteth shalbee a&#173;
bridged of the fore&#173;
sayde money whych 
was to be leuied. But 
if hee haue oone more 
wast then the foresaid 
summe of mony which 
was to bee leuyed a&#173;
mounteth, the other 
shall be discharged by 
and by all the sayd 
money, and shall re&#173;
couer the lande, and 
for the superfluity of 
the wast made aboue 
that that amounteth 
</page>
 
<page sig="202v">
to the saide summe, he 
shall recouer hys da&#173;
mages single, and the 
same lawe is of hys 
executours, and also 
of him that hath his 
estate. And note that 
if hee alyen in fee, for 
terme of lyfe, or in 
taile all or parcell of 
the land which he hol&#173;
deth by Elegit, if the 
alienation be made <expan type="w+t">with</expan>&#173;
in the terme or after, 
hee which hath right 
shall haue against him 
one assise of nouel dis&#173;
seisin. And they both 
must be put in the as&#173;
sise the alyenour &#38; the 
alyenee, and notwith&#173;
standinge that the a&#173;
lienor by pres<expan type="e+_">en</expan>tly, yet 
he which hath right 
shal haue an assise a&#173;
gainst <expan type="y+e">the</expan> alienee alone 
as if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> alienor had ben 
a plain ten<expan type="a+_">an</expan>t for term 
of yeres, &#38; that is by 
the equity of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> statute 
of w. 2. ca. 25. for that 
</page>
 
<page sig="203r">
that he hath not but a 
chattel in effect, and <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
same law is of his ex&#173;
ecutours and of him 
which hath his estate 
as is aforesaid. 
 
And note wel that 
in an Elegit, if the 
sherife returne that he 
had nothinge the daye 
of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> reconizance made 
but that he purchased 
lands after the time, 
then the party plain&#173;
tife shal haue a newe 
writte to haue execu&#173;
tion thereof, the same 
lawe is of a statute 
marchant. And note 
wel that after a fyery 
facyas a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan> may haue 
the Elegit, but not 
contrarie wise, for so 
much that the elegit 
is of more higher na&#173;
ture then the fiery fa&#173;
cias. And note wel <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
if a man recouer by a 
writt of debt and su&#173;
eth a fiery facyas, and 
the sherife return that 
the partye hath no&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="203v">
thing whereof he may 
make gree with <expan type="y+e">the</expan> par&#173;
ty, then <expan type="y+e">the</expan> plaintife shal 
haue a <term lang="la">capias sicut ali&#173;
as, &#38; a pluries</term>, and if 
the sherife returne at 
the <term lang="la">capias mitto vobis 
corpus</term>, &#38; he haue no&#173;
thing where of he may 
make gree to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> partye, 
he shall be sent to the 
prison of the Fleete. &#38; 
there shal abide till he 
haue made agreement 
<expan type="w+t">with</expan> the party, &#38; if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> she&#173;
rife returne <term lang="la">non est in&#173;
uentus</term> then there shall 
go forth an exigent a&#173;
gainst him. And note 
wel <expan type="y+t">that</expan> in a writ of debt 
brought against a per&#173;
son of holy Church, 
which hath nothinge 
of lay fee, &#38; the sherife 
returneth, <expan type="y+t">that</expan> hee hath 
nought by which hee 
may be summoned, th<expan type="e+_">en</expan>
shal the plaintife sue a 
writ to the Bishoppe 
that he make his clerk 
to come, and the Bi&#173;
shop shall make him to 
</page>
 
<page sig="204r">
come by sequestration 
of the Church. And 
note well, that if a m<expan type="a+_">an</expan>
bring a writ of debte 
&#38; recouer, &#38; make hys 
executors &#38; dieth, they 
shall haue execution 
notwithstanding that 
it be within the yeare 
by a fieri facias.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="statute merchant(n)">&#182; Statute merchant.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="obligee(n)" lexeme="recognizee(n)">TO holde by Sta&#173;
tute merchaunt, is 
where a man knowle&#173;
geth to paye certayne 
money to another at a 
certaine day before the 
maior, bailife, or other 
warden of any towne 
<expan type="y+t">that</expan> hath power to make 
execution of the same 
statute, &#38; if the obligee 
pay not the debt at the 
day, &#38; nothing of hys 
goods, landes, or tene&#173;
mentes may be founde 
within the warde of 
the maior or warden 
beforesaide, but in o&#173;
ther places wythout, 
</page>
 
<page sig="204v">
then <expan type="y+e">the</expan> recognisee shall 
sue the recognisaunce 
and obligation with 
a certification to the 
Chauncery vnder the 
kinges seale, and hee 
shall haue out of the 
chauncery a capias to 
the sherife of the co<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
tie where he is to take 
him and to put him in 
prison, if hee bee not a 
clarke, tyll hee haue 
made greement of the 
debt. And one quar&#173;
ter of the yeare after 
that, that hee shall bee 
taken, hee shall haue 
his lande delyuered 
to himselfe to make 
gree to the partye of 
the debt, and hee may 
sel it while hee is in 
prison, and his sale 
shalbee good and law&#173;
full. And if he doo not 
gree <emend err="win"><expan type="w+t">within</expan></emend> a quarter of a 
yere, or if it be retur&#173;
ned <expan type="y+t">that</expan> be not fo<expan type="u+_">un</expan>de, 
then the reconisee may 
haue a writ of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> cha<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
cery which is called 
</page>
 
<page sig="205r">
<term lang="la">Extendi facias</term>, directe to 
al sherifes, where hee 
hath landes, to extend 
his landes and goods, 
&#38; to deliuer the goods 
to him, and to seyse 
him in his landes, to 
holde them to him and 
to his heires and his 
assignes, till that the 
debtes bee leuyed or 
payed, &#38; for that time 
he is tenaunt by sta&#173;
tute merchaunt. And 
note well, that in a 
statute merchaunt the 
reconisee shal haue ex&#173;
ecution of al the lands 
which the reconisour 
had the day of the re&#173;
cognisaunce made, and 
any time after by force 
of the same statute. 
 
And note well, that 
when any wast or des&#173;
truction is made by 
the reconisee, his exe&#173;
cutors, or by him that 
hath estate, the reco&#173;
nisour or hys execu&#173;
tours shall haue the 
same law as is before&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="205v">
saide of the tenant by 
Elegit. 
 
And note wel, if the 
tenaunt by statute 
marchant holde ouer 
his terme, hee that 
hath right maye sue 
against him a <term lang="la">Venire 
facias ad computandum</term>
or els enter by &#38; by as 
vp<expan type="o+_">on</expan> <term lang="la">tenat</term> by <term lang="la">Elegit</term>.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="rent service(n)">&#182; Rent seruice</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="rentcharge(n)" lexeme="rent seck(n)" lexeme="cessavit(n)">There be three ma&#173;
ners of rentes, that 
is to saye, Rent ser&#173;
uice Rent charge, and 
Rent secke. Rent ser&#173;
uice is, where a man 
holdeth of an other 
by Fealtye, and for 
to do suit to his court 
and yeldinge to him 
a certaine rent by the 
yeare for al manner 
of seruices. 
 
And note wel that 
if the Lorde bee seised 
of the seruice and rent 
beforesaid, and they be 
behinde, and hee dis&#173;
traine, and the tenant 
rescueth the distresse 
</page>
 
<page sig="206r">
hee may haue assise, or 
a writte of rescous, 
but it is more necessa&#173;
rye for him to haue 
assise then a writt of 
rescous, for that by 
assise he shal recouer 
his rent and his da&#173;
mages, but by a writt 
of rescous he shal not 
recouer but the thing 
and the dammages. 
 
And note wel, that 
if the lorde be not sei&#173;
sed of the rent and 
seruice and they be be&#173;
hinde, and he distreine 
for them, and the te&#173;
nant take againe the 
distresse, he shall not 
haue assise, but a writ 
of rescous, and shall 
not neede to shewe 
hys right. 
 
And note well that 
if the Lorde distreyne 
hys tenaunt in socage 
for Knightes seruice 
whiche is not deny&#173;
ed hym, and auowe 
for the same seruice 
in courte of Recorde 
</page>
 
<page sig="206v">
he shalbe charged by 
the same seruyce by 
Finch. term <term lang="la">Hillarij Anno</term>
xlvj. 
 
And note wel that if 
the lord may not finde 
a distresse by two yere, 
he shall haue against <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
tenaunt a writ of <term lang="la">Ces&#173;
sauit per biennium</term> as it 
appeareth by the sta&#173;
tute of West. 2. ca. 21. 
And if the tenant die 
in the meane time and 
his issue enter, the lord 
shall haue against the 
issue a writt of entre 
vpon the Cessauit, or 
if the tenant alien, the 
lord shall haue against 
the alienne the foresaid 
writ. But if the Lord 
haue issue and die, and 
the tenaunt bee in ar&#173;
rerages of the said r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
and seruice in the time 
of the father of the is&#173;
sue, &#38; not in the time 
of the issue, he may not 
distrain for <expan type="y+e">the</expan> arerages 
in <expan type="y+e">the</expan> time of his father, 
</page>
 
<page sig="207r">
and he shall haue none 
other recouery against 
the tenaunt or any o&#173;
ther, for that that such 
aduantage is geuen by 
the law to the tenant. 
And note wel that r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
seruice is that to the 
which belongeth feal&#173;
tie, but to rent charge 
and rent secke belon&#173;
geth not fealtie, but 
it belongeth to rent 
seruyce of common 
right.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="rent charge(n)">&#182; Rent charge.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="mort d'ancestor(n)" lexeme="purparty(n)">R<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t charge is where 
a man graunteth cer&#173;
taine rent goinge out 
of his landes or tene&#173;
mentes to another in 
fee simple, or in fee 
taile, or for terme of 
life by deede vpon c<expan type="o+_">on</expan>&#173;
dition, that at what 
time the rent bee bee&#173;
hinde, it shall be well 
and lawful to <expan type="y+e">the</expan> gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
tee to his heires or as&#173;
signes to distrayne in 
</page>
 
<page sig="207v">
the same landes or te&#173;
nements. And note 
well, that if the rent 
bee behinde, it is well 
lawfull to the graun&#173;
tee at his election to 
haue a writ of Annu&#173;
itie, or els he may dis&#173;
train, &#38; if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> distres bee 
taken against his wil 
from him, and he was 
neuer seised before, hee 
hath no recouery but 
by writ of Rescous, 
for the distres first ta&#173;
ken geueth not to him 
seisin, onely if he happ 
the rent before, for if 
he were seised of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
before, &#38; after the rent 
be beh<expan type="i+_">in</expan>d, &#38; he distrain, 
&#38; rescous to him bee 
made, he shal haue ass. 
or a writ of rescous, 
 
And note well, that 
in euerie Assise of 
rent charge and annu&#173;
all rent, or in a writ 
of Annuitie, it bee&#173;
houeth to hym that 
bringeth the writt to 
</page>
 
<page sig="208r">
shewe foorth an espe&#173;
cyaltye, or els hee 
shall not maynetayne 
the Assise, but in a 
Mortdauncestour or 
Forme<emend err=""> </emend>done in the dis&#173;
cender or other writs 
(in the which title 
is geeuen or compri&#173;
sed) brought of rent 
charge, or annuell 
Rente, it needeth 
not to shewe especy&#173;
altye. 
 
And note well that 
if a man graunt a rent 
charge to an other, &#38; 
the grauntee purchase 
the halfe of the lande 
whereof the rent is 
going out, al the r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t is 
extinct, and if the gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;
tee release to the gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;
tour parcell of the 
rent, yet al the rent is 
not extincte. 
 
But in rent seruice 
the law is otherwise, 
for notwithstandinge 
that the Lorde hath 
purchased the halfe of 
the lande whereof the 
</page>
 
<page sig="208v">
rent is going out, yet 
the rent is not extinct 
but for the halfe, &#38; the 
cause of the diuersitie 
is, that rent seruice 
may be seuered to one 
porcion, but not rent 
charge. 
 
And note well, that 
if rent charge be gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>&#173;
ted to two iointly, &#38; 
the one release, yet the 
other shall haue the 
halfe of the rent. And 
also if one purchase <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
halfe of <expan type="y+e">the</expan> land where&#173;
of the rent is goinge 
out, the other shall 
haue <expan type="y+e">the</expan> half of the rent 
of his compainion: &#38; 
if <expan type="y+e">the</expan> disseisor charge <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
land to stra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ger, &#38; the 
disseisie bring as assise 
&#38; recouer, the charge 
is defeated. But if hee 
<expan type="y+t">that</expan> hath right charge <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
land, &#38; a str<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ger faine 
a false action against 
him, and recouer by 
defaut. the charge a&#173;
bydeth. And note 
well, that in case that 
</page>
 
<page sig="209r">
purpartie be betwene 
ij. parceners, and more 
land be allotted to one 
then to the other, and 
shee that hath more of 
the land, chargeth her 
land to the other, and 
she happeth the rent, 
she shal maintein As&#173;
sise without especial&#173;
tie. And if the gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>tee 
haue in fee simple, or in 
fee taile, &#38; hath issue &#38; 
dyeth, if the issue bring 
a Formedon, or assise 
of Mortdauncester, he 
shall neuer be charged 
to shew an especialty.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="rent seck(n)">&#182; Rent secke.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="averrable(a)" lexeme="aiel(n)" lexeme="besaiel(n)">REnt seck, is where 
a man holdeth of me 
by homage, fealtie, &#38; 
other seruice, yelding 
to me a certeine rent 
by the yeare, and I 
graunt this rent to an 
other, reseruing to me 
the seruice. 
 
And note well, that 
in r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t seck, if a man be 
</page>
 
<page sig="209v">
seised of the rent, and 
the rent be behind, hee 
may not distreine, but 
he shall haue assise of 
nouel disseisine. 
 
And note wel that if 
rent seck be gr<expan type="a+_">an</expan>ted to 
man and to his heirs 
and the rent bee bee&#173;
hinde, and the gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
tour dye, the heire 
may not distrein, nor 
shall recouer the ar&#173;
rereges of the tyme 
of his father, as it 
is beefore saide of rent 
seruice. 
 
And in the same 
manner it is to saye 
of Rent charge, or 
annuell rent. But 
in all these rentes 
beefore saide the heire 
maye haue for the 
arrerages in his own 
tyme such aduaun&#173;
tage as his father had 
in his life. 
 
And note well, that 
in r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t seck if a man be 
not seised of the rent, &#38; 
it be behind he is <expan type="w+t">with</expan>out 
</page>
 
<page sig="210r">
recouery, for that that 
it was his own folly 
at <expan type="y+e">the</expan> <emend err="beginniuge">beginninge</emend> when 
the rent was gra<expan type="u+_">un</expan>ted 
to him, or reserued, <expan type="y+t">that</expan>
he toke not seisin of <expan type="y+e">the</expan>
rent as a pennye or 
two pence. And note 
wel that a man maye 
not haue a <term lang="la">Cessauit per 
biennium</term>, or an other 
writte of entrye sur 
<term lang="la">Cessauit</term> for no rent 
seck behinde by two 
yeares, but onely for 
rent seruice, as it ap&#173;
peareth in the statute. 
 
And note wel that 
in rent secke it beeho&#173;
ueth hym that sueth 
for the rent secke for 
to shewe a deede to 
the tenaunt, or els the 
tenaunt shall not bee 
charged with the rent 
but where the rent 
secke was rent seruice 
before, as in this case 
lord, mesne, and te&#173;
naunt, and euerye of 
them holdeth of other 
by homage and fealty 
</page>
 
<page sig="210v">
and the tenant of the 
Mesne x. s. of rent, 
the Lorde paramont 
purchaseth the landes 
or tenem<expan type="e+_">en</expan>ts of the te&#173;
nant, all the seigniory 
of the Mesne but the 
rent is extinct. And 
for this cause this r<expan type="e+_">en</expan>t 
is become rent secke, &#38; 
the rent seruice cha<expan type="u+_">un</expan>&#173;
ged, for hee may not 
distrain for this rent, 
&#38; in this case hee that 
dem<expan type="a+_">an</expan>deth the rent shal 
neuer bee charged to 
shew a deede. Also in 
a writ of Mordaun&#173;
cester, Ayle, or besaile 
of rent seck, it needeth 
not to shew a special&#173;
tie, for <expan type="y+t">that</expan> these writtes 
of possession do com&#173;
prehend a title within 
them selues, that ys 
to say, that the aun&#173;
cestour was seised of 
the same rent, &#38; con&#173;
tinued his possessyon, 
because of which sey&#173;
sin the law supposeth 
<expan type="y+t">that</expan> it is also auerable by 
</page>
 
<page sig="211r">
the Countrey. Yet 
learne, for some sup&#173;
pose that it behoueth 
of necessitie to shewe 
forth a deede, for that 
that rent secke ys a 
thing against common 
right, aswell as rent 
charge. But in Assise 
of Nouel disseisin, &#38; in 
a writ of <term lang="fr">Entre sur dis&#173;
seisin</term> brought of rent 
secke, it behoueth of 
necessity to shew forth 
a deede, for that that 
rent seck is a thing a&#173;
gainst a c<expan type="o+_">om</expan>mon right, 
except in the case be&#173;
fore saide, where it 
was rent seruice be&#173;
fore. And Assise of 
<term lang="fr">Nouel disseisin</term>, &#38; a writ 
of <term lang="fr">entre sur disseisin</term>, con&#173;
teine within them no 
title, but suppose a 
disseisin to be done to 
<expan type="y+e">the</expan> plaintif, &#38; of the en&#173;
tendement of the law, 
the disseisin geueth no 
cause of auerrement a&#173;
gainst common right, 
but of necessitie it be&#173;
</page>
 
<page sig="211v">
hooueth to shew forth 
a deede.</xpln></wordentry>
 
<wordentry type="h"><form lang="en" lexeme="suit(n)" lexeme="service(n)">&#182; Suit seruice.</form>
<xpln lang="en" lexeme="suit real(n)">Suit seruice is to 
come to the Court 
from iij. weekes to iij. 
weekes by the whole 
yeare, and for that a 
man shalbe distrayned 
&#38; not amerced. 
 
Suit real is to come 
to the Court of leete, 
and that is not but ij. 
times in the yere, &#38; for 
that a man shalbe a&#173;
merced, and not 
distrayned.</xpln></wordentry>
